      <p>This article provides an overview of <b>marital rape laws by country</b>. </p>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Introduction">Introduction</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Marital_rape_laws_by_country&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Introduction">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Marital_rape" title="Marital rape">Marital rape</a> is criminalised in many countries. Throughout history until the 1970s, most states granted a husband the right to have sex with his wife whenever he so desired, as part of the <a href="/wiki/Marriage_contract" class="mw-redirect" title="Marriage contract">marriage contract</a>. However, in the 20th century and <a href="/wiki/Second-wave_feminism" title="Second-wave feminism">especially since the 1970s</a>, <a href="/wiki/Women%27s_rights" title="Women's rights">women's rights</a> groups initiated the <a href="/wiki/Anti-rape_movement" title="Anti-rape movement">anti-rape movement</a>, demanding that they be given <a href="/wiki/Sexual_consent" title="Sexual consent">sexual autonomy</a> over their own bodies, including within marriage.<sup id="cite_ref-Randall_1-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Randall-1">[1]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Walby_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Walby-2">[2]</a></sup> These rights have increasingly been recognised,<sup id="cite_ref-Randall_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Randall-1">[1]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Walby_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Walby-2">[2]</a></sup> and consequently marital rape has been criminalised by about 150 countries as of 2019. In some cases, marital rape is explicitly criminalised, in other cases the law makes no distinction between rape by one's husband or rape by anyone else.<sup id="cite_ref-Walby_2-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Walby-2">[2]</a></sup> In a few countries, marital rape was criminalised due to a court decision.<sup id="cite_ref-Randall_1-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Randall-1">[1]</a></sup> In some countries, the prevailing logic goes that there is no such thing as 'marital rape', since the verb 'to <a href="/wiki/Rape" title="Rape">rape</a>' (Latin: <i><a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/rapio#Latin" class="extiw" title="wikt:rapio">rapere</a></i>) originally meant 'to steal' or 'to seize and carry off' (although its meaning shifted during the <a href="/wiki/Middle_Ages" title="Middle Ages">Middle Ages</a> to 'violently abducting a woman for the purpose of forced <a href="/wiki/Sexual_intercourse" title="Sexual intercourse">coitus</a>'<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup>), and it is impossible to steal something you already 'own', and a husband 'owns' his wife in marriage.<sup id="cite_ref-Randall_1-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Randall-1">[1]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>48</span></sup> However, in a few of those countries that do not criminalise marital rape, such as <a href="/wiki/Malaysia" title="Malaysia">Malaysia</a>, a husband can still be punished if he uses violence (and intimidation) in order to have sex with his wife.<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="A">A</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Marital_rape_laws_by_country&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: A">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <table class="sortable wikitable"> 
       <tbody>
        <tr> 
         <th>Country </th> 
         <th>Criminalised </th> 
         <th class="unsortable">Notes </th>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Afghanistan" title="Afghanistan">Afghanistan</a> </td> 
         <td style="background:#F99;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-no">No<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesafghanistan2017_Afghanistan]_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesafghanistan2017_Afghanistan]-5">[5]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124155httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017sca277275htm_Afghanistan]_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124155httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017sca277275htm_Afghanistan]-6">[6]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>The 2009 Law on Elimination of Violence against Women (EVAW) does not exclude spousal rape in its section on Sexual Assault.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">[law 1]</a></sup> However, Article 134 (2) of the <a href="/wiki/Shia_Personal_Status_Law" title="Shia Personal Status Law">Shia Personal Status Law</a> states "It is the duty of the wife to defer to her husband's inclination for sexual enjoyment".<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">[law 2]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Albania" title="Albania">Albania</a> </td> 
         <td style="background:#9F9;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-yes">Explicitly criminalised<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesalbania2017_Albania]_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesalbania2017_Albania]-9">[7]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>The Criminal Code was amended in 2012 and 2013 to criminalise marital rape.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">[8]</a></sup> (Article 102.)<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">[law 3]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Algeria" title="Algeria">Algeria</a> </td> 
         <td style="background:#F99;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-no">No<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEThe_State_of_African_Women2018160_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEThe_State_of_African_Women2018160-12">[9]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>The law criminalises rape but does not address spousal rape.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124201httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017nea277235htm_Algeria]_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124201httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017nea277235htm_Algeria]-13">[10]</a></sup> The Penal Code does not explicitly excludes marital rape from the definition of rape,<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">[law 4]</a></sup> however the <a href="/wiki/Algerian_Family_Code" title="Algerian Family Code">Algerian Family Code</a> requires a wife to obey her husband<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">[11]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Andorra" title="Andorra">Andorra</a> </td> 
         <td style="background:#9F9;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-yes">Yes<sup id="cite_ref-Analytical_study_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Analytical_study-16">[12]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>Rape, including spousal rape can be punished by up to 15 years imprisonment.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124204httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017eur277135htm_Andorra]_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124204httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017eur277135htm_Andorra]-17">[13]</a></sup> The Penal Code does not exclude marital rape from its definition of rape (Article 145).<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">[law 5]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Angola" title="Angola">Angola</a> </td> 
         <td style="background:#9F9;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-yes">Explicitly criminalised<sup id="cite_ref-SADC_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SADC-19">[14]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>Rape, including spousal rape, is illegal and punishable by up to eight years’ imprisonment.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124207httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017af276967htm_Angola]_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124207httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017af276967htm_Angola]-20">[15]</a></sup> Article 170 of the Código Penal explicitly includes a spouse in its definition of rape.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">[law 6]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Antigua_and_Barbuda" title="Antigua and Barbuda">Antigua and Barbuda</a><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesantigua-and-barbuda2017_Antigua_and_Barbuda]_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesantigua-and-barbuda2017_Antigua_and_Barbuda]-22">[16]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td style="background:#F99;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-no">Explicitly excluded<sup id="cite_ref-Postcolonial_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Postcolonial-23">[17]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>Article 3 (1) of the Sexual Offences Act, 1995, includes in the definition of rape: "with a female person who is not his wife".<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">[law 7]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Argentina" title="Argentina">Argentina</a> </td> 
         <td style="background:#9F9;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-yes">Explicitly criminalised<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesargentina2017_Argentina]_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesargentina2017_Argentina]-25">[18]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>Rape of men and women, including spousal rape, can be punished by imprisonment from six months to up to 20 years.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124215httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017wha277303htm_Argentina]_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124215httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017wha277303htm_Argentina]-26">[19]</a></sup> Spousal rape is criminalised by Article 5 (3) of the Law of Comprehensive Protection of Women (Ley de Protección Integral s las Mujeres), 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">[law 8]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Armenia" title="Armenia">Armenia</a> </td> 
         <td style="background:#9F9;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-yes">Yes<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesarmenia2017_Armenia]_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesarmenia2017_Armenia]-28">[20]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>Rape is a criminal offense, and conviction carries a maximum sentence of 15 years; general rape statutes (Article 138 of the Criminal Code)<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">[law 9]</a></sup> applied to the prosecution of spousal rape.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124219httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017eur277137htm_Armenia]_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124219httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017eur277137htm_Armenia]-30">[21]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">Australia</a> </td> 
         <td style="background:#9F9;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-yes">Explicitly criminalised<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesaustralia2017_Australia]_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesaustralia2017_Australia]-31">[22]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>Criminalisation in Australia began with the state of <a href="/wiki/New_South_Wales" title="New South Wales">New South Wales</a> in 1981, followed by all other states from 1985 to 1992.<sup id="cite_ref-Temkin86_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Temkin86-32">[23]</a></sup> The government enforced the law effectively. The laws of individual states and territories provide the penalties for rape.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124221httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017eap277065htm_Australia]_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124221httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017eap277065htm_Australia]-33">[24]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Austria" title="Austria">Austria</a> </td> 
         <td style="background:#9F9;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-yes">Yes<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesaustria2017_Austria]_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesaustria2017_Austria]-34">[25]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>Spousal rape can be punished by up to 15 years imprisonment,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124223httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017eur277139htm_Austria]_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124223httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017eur277139htm_Austria]-35">[26]</a></sup> and was first criminalised in 1989.<sup id="cite_ref-coe_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-coe-36">[27]</a></sup> The Criminal Code (§ 201) does not explicitly excludes marital rape from the definition of rape.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">[law 10]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Azerbaijan" title="Azerbaijan">Azerbaijan</a> </td> 
         <td style="background:#9F9;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-yes">Yes<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesazerbaijan2017_Azerbaijan]_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesazerbaijan2017_Azerbaijan]-38">[28]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>Spousal rape is illegal, but observers stated police did not effectively investigate such claims.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124226httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017eur277141htm_Azerbaijan]_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124226httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017eur277141htm_Azerbaijan]-39">[29]</a></sup> The Criminal Code does not exclude marital rape from its definition of rape (Articles 108, 149).<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">[law 11]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr>
       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="B">B</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Marital_rape_laws_by_country&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: B">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <table class="sortable wikitable"> 
       <tbody>
        <tr> 
         <th>Country </th> 
         <th>Criminalised </th> 
         <th class="unsortable">Notes </th>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/The_Bahamas" title="The Bahamas">The Bahamas</a><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesbahamas-the2017_The_Bahamas]_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesbahamas-the2017_The_Bahamas]-41">[30]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td style="background:#F99;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-no">Explicitly excluded<sup id="cite_ref-Postcolonial_23-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Postcolonial-23">[17]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>Rape of men or women is illegal, but the law does not protect against spousal rape, except if the couple is separated or in the process of divorce, or if there is a restraining order in place.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124229httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017wha277305htm_The_Bahamas]_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124229httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017wha277305htm_The_Bahamas]-42">[31]</a></sup> Section 3 of the Sexual Offences Act, 2010, includes "person who is not his spouse" in the definition of rape.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">[law 12]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Bahrain" title="Bahrain">Bahrain</a><sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">[32]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td style="background:#F99;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-no">Explicitly excluded<sup id="cite_ref-BahrainLaw_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BahrainLaw-45">[law 13]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>Rape is illegal, although the criminal code allows an alleged rapist to marry his victim to avoid punishment. The law does not address spousal rape.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124231httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017nea277237htm_Bahrain]_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124231httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017nea277237htm_Bahrain]-46">[33]</a></sup> Article 353 of the Penal Code explicitly excludes spousal rape.<sup id="cite_ref-BahrainLaw_45-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BahrainLaw-45">[law 13]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Bangladesh" title="Bangladesh">Bangladesh</a> </td> 
         <td style="background:#F99;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-no">No<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesbangladesh2017_Bangladesh]_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesbangladesh2017_Bangladesh]-47">[34]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>The law prohibits rape of a female by a male and physical spousal abuse, but the law excludes marital rape if the female is above 13.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124234httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017sca277277htm_Bangladesh]_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124234httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017sca277277htm_Bangladesh]-48">[35]</a></sup> Section 375 (Of Rape) of the Penal Code includes the exception: "Sexual intercourse by a man with his own wife, the wife not being under thirteen years of age, is not rape."<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">[law 14]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Barbados" title="Barbados">Barbados</a><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesbarbados2017_Barbados]_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesbarbados2017_Barbados]-50">[36]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td style="background:#9F9;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-yes">Explicitly criminalised<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">[37]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>The Sexual Offences (Amendment) Act 2016 modified section 3 (4) of the Sexual Offences Act 1992, removing the previous "marital exemption" and replacing it with explicit criminalisation of marital rape.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">[law 15]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">[38]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Belarus" title="Belarus">Belarus</a> </td> 
         <td style="background:#9F9;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-yes">Yes<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesbelarus2017_Belarus]_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesbelarus2017_Belarus]-54">[39]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>Article 166 of the Criminal Code<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">[law 16]</a></sup> criminalises rape in general but does not include separate provisions on marital rape.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124239httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017eur277143htm_Belarus]_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124239httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017eur277143htm_Belarus]-56">[40]</a></sup> Prosecutions for marital rape are rare and it is often regarded as a private rather than criminal issue.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">[41]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Belgium" title="Belgium">Belgium</a> </td> 
         <td style="background:#9F9;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-yes">Yes<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesbelgium2017_Belgium]_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesbelgium2017_Belgium]-58">[42]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>Marital rape was criminalised by court decision in 1979.<sup id="cite_ref-Cornell_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cornell-59">[43]</a></sup> The criminal code was amended in 1989 to treat marital rape the same as other forms of rape.<sup id="cite_ref-coe.int_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-coe.int-60">[44]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-UNIFEM-2003_61-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UNIFEM-2003-61">[45]</a></sup> (Code Pénal Art. 375)<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">[law 17]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Belize" title="Belize">Belize</a> </td> 
         <td style="background:#9F9;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-yes">Explicitly criminalised<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesbelize2017_Belize]_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesbelize2017_Belize]-63">[46]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>Article 46 of the Criminal Code<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">[law 18]</a></sup> criminalises rape of men or women, including spousal rape. The code states that a person convicted of rape shall be sentenced to imprisonment for eight years to life.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124244httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017wha277309htm_Belize]_65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124244httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017wha277309htm_Belize]-65">[47]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Benin" title="Benin">Benin</a><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEThe_State_of_African_Women2018146_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEThe_State_of_African_Women2018146-66">[48]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td style="background:#9F9;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-yes">Explicitly criminalised<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesbenin2017_Benin]_67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesbenin2017_Benin]-67">[49]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>Article 2 of the 2011 Law <i>Portant prévention et répression des violences faites aux femmes</i> (For prevention and repression of violence against women),<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">[law 19]</a></sup> explicitly prohibits spousal rape and provides the maximum penalty of 5 years imprisonment for conviction of raping a domestic partner.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124246httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017af276969htm_Benin]_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124246httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017af276969htm_Benin]-69">[50]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Bhutan" title="Bhutan">Bhutan</a> </td> 
         <td style="background:#9F9;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-yes">Explicitly criminalised<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesbhutan2017_Bhutan]_70-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesbhutan2017_Bhutan]-70">[51]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>Spousal rape is illegal and prosecuted as a misdemeanor.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124248httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017sca277279htm_Bhutan]_71-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124248httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017sca277279htm_Bhutan]-71">[52]</a></sup> (Penal Code Sec. 199 &amp; 200)<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">[law 20]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Bolivia" title="Bolivia">Bolivia</a> </td> 
         <td style="background:#9F9;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-yes">Explicitly criminalised<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesbolivia2017_Bolivia]_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesbolivia2017_Bolivia]-73">[53]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>In 2013 the government passed the Law Guaranteeing Women a Life Free from Violence (Ley Integral Para Garantizar A Las Mujeres Una Vida Libre De Violencia).<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124251httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017wha277311htm_Bolivia]_74-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124251httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017wha277311htm_Bolivia]-74">[54]</a></sup> It's provisions included the repeal of the marital rape exemption in the Penal Code,<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">[55]</a></sup> and making rape by a spouse an aggravating factor when sentencing, extending imprisonment by 5 years.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">[law 21]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Bosnia_and_Herzegovina" title="Bosnia and Herzegovina">Bosnia and Herzegovina</a> </td> 
         <td style="background:#9F9;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-yes">Yes<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesbosnia-and-herzegovina2017_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina]_77-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesbosnia-and-herzegovina2017_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina]-77">[56]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>The maximum penalty for rape, regardless of gender, including spousal rape, is 15 years in prison. The failure of police to treat spousal rape as a serious offense inhibited the effective enforcement of the law.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124254httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017eur277147htm_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina]_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124254httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017eur277147htm_Bosnia_and_Herzegovina]-78">[57]</a></sup> The 2003 Penal Code removed "marital exemption" from Article 203 (Rape).<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">[law 22]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Botswana" title="Botswana">Botswana</a><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEThe_State_of_African_Women2018157_80-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEThe_State_of_African_Women2018157-80">[58]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Stefiszyn_81-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Stefiszyn-81">[59]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td style="background:#F99;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-no">Customary law<sup id="cite_ref-The_State_of_African_Women_82-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_State_of_African_Women-82">[60]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>The law criminalises rape but does not recognize spousal rape as a crime.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124256httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017af276971htm_Botswana]_83-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124256httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017af276971htm_Botswana]-83">[61]</a></sup> Customary law holds that sex within marriage is consensual.<sup id="cite_ref-The_State_of_African_Women_82-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_State_of_African_Women-82">[60]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Brazil</a> </td> 
         <td style="background:#9F9;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-yes">Explicitly criminalised<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesbrazil2017_Brazil]_84-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesbrazil2017_Brazil]-84">[62]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>Since 2005,<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">[law 23]</a></sup> the law criminalises rape of men or women, including spousal rape.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124258httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017wha277313htm_Brazil]_86-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124258httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017wha277313htm_Brazil]-86">[63]</a></sup> (Articles 213 &amp; 226 of the Criminal Code)<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">[law 24]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Brunei" title="Brunei">Brunei</a> </td> 
         <td style="background:#F99;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-no">Explicitly excluded<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesbrunei-darussalam2017_Brunei_Darussalam]_88-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesbrunei-darussalam2017_Brunei_Darussalam]-88">[64]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>The law does not criminalise spousal rape and Article 375 of the Penal Code<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">[law 25]</a></sup> explicitly states that sexual intercourse by a man with his wife is not rape, as long as she is not younger than 13 years.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124301httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017eap277067htm_Brunei]_90-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124301httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017eap277067htm_Brunei]-90">[65]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">[66]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Bulgaria" title="Bulgaria">Bulgaria</a> </td> 
         <td style="background:#9F9;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-yes">Yes<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesbulgaria2017_Bulgaria]_92-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesbulgaria2017_Bulgaria]-92">[67]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>The law criminalises rape (Article 152 of the Criminal Code).<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">[law 26]</a></sup> While authorities could prosecute spousal rape under the general rape statute, they rarely did so.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124303httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017eur277149htm_Bulgaria]_94-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124303httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017eur277149htm_Bulgaria]-94">[68]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Burkina_Faso" title="Burkina Faso">Burkina Faso</a><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEThe_State_of_African_Women2018146_66-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEThe_State_of_African_Women2018146-66">[48]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td style="background:#9F9;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-yes">Explicitly criminalised<sup id="cite_ref-Burkina_Faso_95-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Burkina_Faso-95">[69]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>In 2015 the government passed the Law on the Prevention and Repression of Violence Against Women and Girls and Support for Victims. Conviction of rape is punishable by five to 10 years’ imprisonment.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">[70]</a></sup> Marital rape is covered by this law.<sup id="cite_ref-Burkina_Faso_95-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Burkina_Faso-95">[69]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Burundi" title="Burundi">Burundi</a> </td> 
         <td style="background:#9F9;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-yes">Explicitly criminalised<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesburundi2017_Burundi]_97-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesburundi2017_Burundi]-97">[71]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>Spousal rape was criminalised in 2016 by the <i>Loi N° 1/13 du 22 septembre 2016 portant prévention, protection des victimes et répression des Violences Basées sur le Genre</i> (Articles 2i &amp; 27),<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">[law 27]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesburundi2017_Burundi]_97-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesburundi2017_Burundi]-97">[71]</a></sup> with penalties of up to 30 years’ imprisonment. The government did not enforce the law uniformly, and rape and other domestic and sexual violence continued to be serious problems.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124311httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017af276975htm_Burundi]_99-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124311httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017af276975htm_Burundi]-99">[72]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr>
       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="C">C</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Marital_rape_laws_by_country&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: C">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <table class="sortable wikitable"> 
       <tbody>
        <tr> 
         <th>Country </th> 
         <th>Criminalised </th> 
         <th class="unsortable">Notes </th>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Cameroon" title="Cameroon">Cameroon</a><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEThe_State_of_African_Women2018152_100-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEThe_State_of_African_Women2018152-100">[73]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td style="background:#F99;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-no">Customary law<sup id="cite_ref-Cameroon_101-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cameroon-101">[74]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-cr1_102-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cr1-102">[75]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>The law does not address spousal rape,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124320httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017af276979htm_Cameroon]_103-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124320httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017af276979htm_Cameroon]-103">[76]</a></sup> but does not exclude marital rape. Judges accept the principle husbands have "disciplinary rights" over their wives, including when they refuse to have sexual relations.<sup id="cite_ref-Cameroon_101-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cameroon-101">[74]</a></sup> It is also accepted that during marriage the woman implicitly consents to sexual intercourse whenever the husband wishes.<sup id="cite_ref-cr1_102-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cr1-102">[75]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canada</a> </td> 
         <td style="background:#9F9;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-yes">Explicitly criminalised<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiescanada2017_Canada]_104-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiescanada2017_Canada]-104">[77]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>Articles 271 &amp; 278 of the Criminal Code<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">[law 28]</a></sup> criminalise rape of men or women, including spousal rape, as sexual assault, and the government enforced the law effectively.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124322httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017wha277315htm_Canada]_106-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124322httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017wha277315htm_Canada]-106">[78]</a></sup> Marital rape was first criminalised in 1983.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">[79]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">[80]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Cambodia" title="Cambodia">Cambodia</a> </td> 
         <td style="background:#9F9;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-yes">Yes<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiescambodia2017_Cambodia]_109-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiescambodia2017_Cambodia]-109">[81]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>Spousal rape is not specifically mentioned in the penal code (articles 239-245),<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">[law 29]</a></sup> but the underlying conduct can be prosecuted as “rape,” “causing injury,” or “indecent assault.” Charges for spousal rape under the penal code and the domestic violence law were rare.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124317httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017eap277071htm_Cambodia]_111-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124317httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017eap277071htm_Cambodia]-111">[82]</a></sup> Marital rape was criminalised in 2005.<sup id="cite_ref-CAT-Cambodia_112-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CAT-Cambodia-112">[83]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Cape_Verde" title="Cape Verde">Cape Verde</a><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEThe_State_of_African_Women2018146_66-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEThe_State_of_African_Women2018146-66">[48]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td style="background:#9F9;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-yes">Explicitly criminalised<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiescabo-verde2017_Cabo_Verde]_113-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiescabo-verde2017_Cabo_Verde]-113">[84]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>Spousal rape is implicitly covered by the 2001 gender-based violence law;<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">[law 30]</a></sup> penalties for conviction range from one to five years’ imprisonment.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124314httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017af276977htm_Cabo_Verde]_115-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124314httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017af276977htm_Cabo_Verde]-115">[85]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Central_African_Republic" title="Central African Republic">Central African Republic</a><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEThe_State_of_African_Women2018152_100-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEThe_State_of_African_Women2018152-100">[73]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-UN_2011_Report_116-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UN_2011_Report-116">[86]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">[87]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td style="background:#F99;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-no">Customary law<sup id="cite_ref-The_State_of_African_Women_82-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_State_of_African_Women-82">[60]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>The law prohibits rape, although it does not specifically prohibit spousal rape.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124325httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017af276981htm_Central_African_Republic]_118-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124325httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017af276981htm_Central_African_Republic]-118">[88]</a></sup> Customary law holds that sex within marriage is consensual.<sup id="cite_ref-The_State_of_African_Women_82-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_State_of_African_Women-82">[60]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Chad_(country)" class="mw-redirect" title="Chad (country)">Chad</a><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEThe_State_of_African_Women2018152_100-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEThe_State_of_African_Women2018152-100">[73]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-UN_2011_Report_116-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UN_2011_Report-116">[86]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td style="background:#F99;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-no">Customary law<sup id="cite_ref-The_State_of_African_Women_82-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_State_of_African_Women-82">[60]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>The law does not specifically address spousal rape.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124328httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017af276983htm_Chad]_119-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124328httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017af276983htm_Chad]-119">[89]</a></sup> Customary law holds that sex within marriage is consensual.<sup id="cite_ref-The_State_of_African_Women_82-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_State_of_African_Women-82">[60]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Chile" title="Chile">Chile</a> </td> 
         <td style="background:#9F9;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-yes">Explicitly criminalised<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomieschile2017_Chile]_120-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomieschile2017_Chile]-120">[90]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>The law criminalises rape of men or women, including spousal rape (Penal Code art. 369).<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">[law 31]</a></sup> Penalties for rape range from five to 15 years’ imprisonment.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124331httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017wha277317htm_Chile]_122-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124331httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017wha277317htm_Chile]-122">[91]</a></sup> Marital rape was criminalised in 1999.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">[92]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/People%27s_Republic_of_China" class="mw-redirect" title="People's Republic of China">China</a> </td> 
         <td style="background:#F99;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-no">No<sup id="cite_ref-UN_2011_Report_116-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UN_2011_Report-116">[86]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">[93]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">[94]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>The law does not safeguard same-sex couples or victims of marital rape.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124334httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017eap277073htm_China_(includes_Tibet,_Hong_Kong,_and_Macau)]_126-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124334httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017eap277073htm_China_(includes_Tibet,_Hong_Kong,_and_Macau)]-126">[95]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Colombia" title="Colombia">Colombia</a> </td> 
         <td style="background:#9F9;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-yes">Explicitly criminalised<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiescolombia2017_Colombia]_127-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiescolombia2017_Colombia]-127">[96]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>Although prohibited by law, rape, including spousal rape (art. 211(5) of Ley 599 de 2000),<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">[law 32]</a></sup> remained a serious problem.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124340httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017wha277319htm_Colombia]_129-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124340httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017wha277319htm_Colombia]-129">[97]</a></sup> Marital rape was criminalised in 1996,<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">[98]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Comoros" title="Comoros">Comoros</a> </td> 
         <td style="background:#9F9;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-yes">Explicitly criminalised<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiescomoros2017_Comoros]_131-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiescomoros2017_Comoros]-131">[99]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>In 2014, Loi N° 14-036/AU dealing with violence against women was promulgated, amongst its provisions (art. 1) was the criminalisation of marital rape.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20170307090213httpswwwstategovdocumentsorganization265452pdf_Comoros]_132-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20170307090213httpswwwstategovdocumentsorganization265452pdf_Comoros]-132">[100]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Democratic_Republic_of_Congo" class="mw-redirect" title="Democratic Republic of Congo">Democratic Republic of Congo</a><sup id="cite_ref-UN_2011_Report_116-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UN_2011_Report-116">[86]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">[101]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td style="background:#F99;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-no">Customary law<sup id="cite_ref-The_State_of_African_Women_82-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_State_of_African_Women-82">[60]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>The legal definition of rape does not include spousal rape.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124347httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017af276987htm_Democratic_Republic_of_Congo]_134-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124347httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017af276987htm_Democratic_Republic_of_Congo]-134">[102]</a></sup> Customary law holds that sex within marriage is consensual.<sup id="cite_ref-The_State_of_African_Women_82-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_State_of_African_Women-82">[60]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Republic of the Congo">Republic of the Congo</a><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEThe_State_of_African_Women2018152_100-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEThe_State_of_African_Women2018152-100">[73]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-UN_2011_Report_116-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UN_2011_Report-116">[86]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td style="background:#F99;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-no">Customary law<sup id="cite_ref-The_State_of_African_Women_82-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_State_of_African_Women-82">[60]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>Customary law holds that sex within marriage is consensual.<sup id="cite_ref-The_State_of_African_Women_82-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_State_of_African_Women-82">[60]</a></sup> Women's rights groups have reported that spousal rape was common.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124350httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017af276989htm_Congo,_Republic_of_the]_135-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124350httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017af276989htm_Congo,_Republic_of_the]-135">[103]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Costa_Rica" title="Costa Rica">Costa Rica</a> </td> 
         <td style="background:#9F9;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-yes">Explicitly criminalised<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiescosta-rica2017_Costa_Rica]_136-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiescosta-rica2017_Costa_Rica]-136">[104]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>The law criminalises rape of men or women, including spousal rape (Ley de Penalización de la Violencia contra las Mujeres No. 8589 art.29)<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">[law 33]</a></sup> and domestic violence, and provides penalties from 10 to 18 years in prison for rape. The judicial branch generally enforced the law.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124353httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017wha277321htm_Costa_Rica]_138-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124353httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017wha277321htm_Costa_Rica]-138">[105]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Croatia" title="Croatia">Croatia</a> </td> 
         <td style="background:#9F9;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-yes">Explicitly criminalised<sup id="cite_ref-coe_36-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-coe-36">[27]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiescroatia2017_Croatia]_139-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiescroatia2017_Croatia]-139">[106]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>Conviction of rape, including spousal rape, is punishable by up to 15 years imprisonment.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124400httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017eur277151htm_Croatia]_140-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124400httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017eur277151htm_Croatia]-140">[107]</a></sup> (Articles 152 &amp; 154(1)(1) of the Criminal Code)<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">[law 34]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Cuba" title="Cuba">Cuba</a><sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">[108]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td style="background:#9F9;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-yes">Explicitly criminalised<sup id="cite_ref-UN_2011_Report_116-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UN_2011_Report-116">[86]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>The law specifically criminalises rape of women, including spousal rape, and separately criminalises “lascivious abuse” against both genders. The government enforced both laws. Penalties for rape are at least four years’ imprisonment.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124403httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017wha277323htm_Cuba]_143-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124403httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017wha277323htm_Cuba]-143">[109]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Cyprus" title="Cyprus">Cyprus</a> </td> 
         <td style="background:#9F9;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-yes">Explicitly criminalised<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiescyprus2017_Cyprus]_144-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiescyprus2017_Cyprus]-144">[110]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>The law criminalises rape, including spousal rape (sec.5 The Family Violence (Prevention and Protection of Victims) Law),<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">[law 35]</a></sup> with a maximum sentence of life in prison for violations. The government enforced the law effectively.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124406httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017eur277153htm_Cyprus]_146-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124406httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017eur277153htm_Cyprus]-146">[111]</a></sup> Marital rape was criminalised in 1994.<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">[112]</a></sup> Spousal rape is also criminalzed in the area administered by Turkish Cypriots (<a href="/wiki/Turkish_Republic_of_Northern_Cyprus" class="mw-redirect" title="Turkish Republic of Northern Cyprus">Turkish Republic of Northern Cyprus</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180421055543httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017eur277155htm_Cyprus_-_the_Area_Administered_by_Turkish_Cypriots]_148-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180421055543httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017eur277155htm_Cyprus_-_the_Area_Administered_by_Turkish_Cypriots]-148">[113]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Czech_Republic" title="Czech Republic">Czech Republic</a> </td> 
         <td style="background:#9F9;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-yes">Yes<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesczech-republic2017_Czech_Republic]_149-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesczech-republic2017_Czech_Republic]-149">[114]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>The law prohibits rape, including spousal rape (although not explicitly), and provides a penalty of two to 15 years in prison for violations.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124414httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017eur277157htm_Czech_Republic]_150-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124414httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017eur277157htm_Czech_Republic]-150">[115]</a></sup> (Section 185 of the Penal Code)<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">[law 36]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr>
       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="D">D</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Marital_rape_laws_by_country&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: D">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <table class="sortable wikitable"> 
       <tbody>
        <tr> 
         <th>Country </th> 
         <th>Criminalised </th> 
         <th class="unsortable">Notes </th>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Denmark" title="Denmark">Denmark</a> </td> 
         <td style="background:#9F9;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-yes">Yes<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesdenmark2017_Denmark]_152-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesdenmark2017_Denmark]-152">[116]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>The law criminalises rape against women or men (the statute is gender neutral), including spousal rape, and domestic violence. Penalties for rape include imprisonment for up to 12 years.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124416httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017eur277159htm_Denmark]_153-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124416httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017eur277159htm_Denmark]-153">[117]</a></sup> (Section 216 of the Criminal Code)<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">[law 37]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Djibouti" title="Djibouti">Djibouti</a> </td> 
         <td style="background:#F99;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-no">No<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEThe_State_of_African_Women2018149_155-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEThe_State_of_African_Women2018149-155">[118]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">[119]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>The law includes sentences of up to 20 years’ imprisonment for rape but does not address spousal rape.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124419httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017af276993htm_Djibouti]_157-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124419httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017af276993htm_Djibouti]-157">[120]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Dominica" title="Dominica">Dominica</a> </td> 
         <td style="background:#9F9;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-yes">Explicitly criminalised<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesdominica2017_Dominica]_158-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesdominica2017_Dominica]-158">[121]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>The Sexual Offences (Amendment) Act 2016 repealed the previous "marital exclusions" of the rape law and introduced a specific marital rape section [s3 (3)] to the Sexual Offences Act.<sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">[law 38]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Dominican_Republic" title="Dominican Republic">Dominican Republic</a> </td> 
         <td style="background:#9F9;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-yes">Explicitly criminalised<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesdominican-republic2017_Dominican_Republic]_160-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesdominican-republic2017_Dominican_Republic]-160">[122]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>The law criminalises rape of men or women, including spousal rape, and other forms of violence against women, such as incest and sexual aggression. The sentences for conviction of rape range from 10 to 15 years in prison and a fine of 100,000 to 200,000 pesos.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124425httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017wha277327htm_Dominican_Republic]_161-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124425httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017wha277327htm_Dominican_Republic]-161">[123]</a></sup> In 1997, Ley 24-97 (Sobre Violencia Intrafamiliar, de Genero y Sexual)<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">[law 39]</a></sup> modified the Penal Code to explicitly criminalise spousal rape (art. 332).<sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">[law 40]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr>
       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="E">E</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Marital_rape_laws_by_country&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: E">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <table class="sortable wikitable"> 
       <tbody>
        <tr> 
         <th>Country </th> 
         <th>Criminalised </th> 
         <th class="unsortable">Notes </th>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/East_Timor" title="East Timor">East Timor</a> </td> 
         <td style="background:#9F9;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-yes">Explicitly criminalised<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiestimor-leste2017_Timor-Leste]_164-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiestimor-leste2017_Timor-Leste]-164">[124]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>Although rape, including marital rape, is a crime punishable by up to 20 years in prison, failures to investigate or prosecute cases of alleged rape and sexual abuse were common.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422125120httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017eap277123htm_Timor-Leste]_165-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422125120httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017eap277123htm_Timor-Leste]-165">[125]</a></sup> In 2010, Article 2(2)b) of Law No. 7/2010 on Domestic Violence, extended the definition of rape (art. 172 of the Criminal Code) to explicitly include marital rape.<sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">[law 41]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">[law 42]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Ecuador" title="Ecuador">Ecuador</a> </td> 
         <td style="background:#9F9;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-yes">Explicitly criminalised<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesecuador2017_Ecuador]_168-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesecuador2017_Ecuador]-168">[126]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>The law criminalises rape of men or women, including spousal rape and domestic violence. Rape is punishable with penalties of up to 22 years in prison.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124428httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017wha277329htm_Ecuador]_169-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124428httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017wha277329htm_Ecuador]-169">[127]</a></sup> (Articles 155-158 of the Código Orgánico Integral Penal).<sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170">[law 43]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Egypt" title="Egypt">Egypt</a><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEThe_State_of_African_Women2018160_12-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEThe_State_of_African_Women2018160-12">[9]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td style="background:#F99;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-no">Case Law<sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171">[128]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>The law prohibits rape, prescribing criminal penalties of 15 to 25 years’ imprisonment, or life imprisonment for cases of rape involving armed abduction. Spousal rape is not illegal,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124431httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017nea277239htm_Egypt]_172-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124431httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017nea277239htm_Egypt]-172">[129]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-UN_2011_Report_116-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UN_2011_Report-116">[86]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Warrick_173-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Warrick-173">[130]</a></sup> based on a 1928 <a href="/wiki/Judiciary_of_Egypt#Courts" title="Judiciary of Egypt">Court of Cassation</a> ruling that <i>"a wife cannot withhold sex from her husband without a valid reason according to <a href="/wiki/Sharia" title="Sharia">sharia</a>".</i><sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">[131]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/El_Salvador" title="El Salvador">El Salvador</a> </td> 
         <td style="background: #ececec; color: #2C2C2C; font-size: smaller; vertical-align: middle; text-align: center;" class="unknown table-unknown">Unclear </td> 
         <td>Marital rape is not specifically addressed by statue. The World Bank's 2018 " "Women, Business and the Law" report states that the country's general rape laws apply to marital rape.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesel-salvador2017_El_Salvador]_175-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesel-salvador2017_El_Salvador]-175">[132]</a></sup> The 2017 El Salvador Country Report on Human Rights Practices suggests this is only at a judge's discretion.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124435httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017wha277331htm_El_Salvador]_176-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124435httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017wha277331htm_El_Salvador]-176">[133]</a></sup> An earlier (2011) report, the "UN Womens Justice Report" states there are no laws covering marital rape.<sup id="cite_ref-UN_2011_Report_116-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UN_2011_Report-116">[86]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Equatorial_Guinea" title="Equatorial Guinea">Equatorial Guinea</a><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEThe_State_of_African_Women2018152_100-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEThe_State_of_African_Women2018152-100">[73]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-UN_2011_Report_116-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UN_2011_Report-116">[86]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td style="background:#F99;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-no">Explicitly excluded<sup id="cite_ref-Kenyan_Woman_177-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kenyan_Woman-177">[134]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>Marital rape is explicitly excluded from the definition of rape within the law.<sup id="cite_ref-Kenyan_Woman_177-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kenyan_Woman-177">[134]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Eritrea" title="Eritrea">Eritrea</a><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEThe_State_of_African_Women2018149_155-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEThe_State_of_African_Women2018149-155">[118]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td style="background:#F99;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-no">Explicitly excluded<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomieseritrea2017_Eritrea]_178-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomieseritrea2017_Eritrea]-178">[135]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>Article 307 of the Penal Code Explicitly excludes marital rape except where spouses are not living together.<sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">[law 44]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Eswatini" title="Eswatini">Eswatini</a> </td> 
         <td style="background:#F99;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-no">Explicitly excluded<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEThe_State_of_African_Women2018157_80-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEThe_State_of_African_Women2018157-80">[58]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomieseswatini2017_Eswatini]_180-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomieseswatini2017_Eswatini]-180">[136]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>The Girls and Women's Protection Act of 1920 explicitly excludes marital rape from criminalisation.<sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181">[137]</a></sup> As of 2018, the Amended Marriage Act, which criminalises marital rape, had not been promulgated by the Government.<sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182">[138]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Ethiopia" title="Ethiopia">Ethiopia</a><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesethiopia2017_Ethiopia]_183-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesethiopia2017_Ethiopia]-183">[139]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FBanda_184-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FBanda-184">[140]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td style="background:#F99;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-no">Explicitly excluded<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEThe_State_of_African_Women2018149_155-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEThe_State_of_African_Women2018149-155">[118]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Kenyan_Woman_177-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kenyan_Woman-177">[134]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>Marital rape is excluded from the definition of rape in Article 620 of the Criminal Code, which limits rape to "outside wedlock".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEThe_State_of_African_Women2018149_155-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEThe_State_of_African_Women2018149-155">[118]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-185" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-185">[law 45]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Estonia" title="Estonia">Estonia</a> </td> 
         <td style="background:#9F9;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-yes">Explicitly criminalised<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesestonia2017_Estonia]_186-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesestonia2017_Estonia]-186">[141]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>The law criminalises rape, including spousal rape (Criminal Code §58(2) &amp; 141),<sup id="cite_ref-187" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-187">[law 46]</a></sup> and physical abuse, including domestic violence. The penalty for rape, including spousal rape, is imprisonment for up to 15 years.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124442httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017eur277161htm_Estonia]_188-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124442httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017eur277161htm_Estonia]-188">[142]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr>
       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="F">F</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Marital_rape_laws_by_country&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: F">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <table class="sortable wikitable"> 
       <tbody>
        <tr> 
         <th>Country </th> 
         <th>Criminalised </th> 
         <th class="unsortable">Notes </th>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Fiji" title="Fiji">Fiji</a><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesfiji2017_Fiji]_189-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesfiji2017_Fiji]-189">[143]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td style="background:#9F9;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-yes">Case Law<sup id="cite_ref-sexualrightsdatabase_Fiji_190-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sexualrightsdatabase_Fiji-190">[144]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>Rape (including spousal rape), domestic abuse, incest, and indecent assault were significant problems; there was a large increase in the reported number of rape cases this year, due at least in part to greater awareness that a spouse can be charged with rape of his/her partner. The law provides for a maximum punishment of life imprisonment for rape.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124449httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017eap277081htm_Fiji]_191-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124449httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017eap277081htm_Fiji]-191">[145]</a></sup> The definition of rape in §207 of the Crimes Decree does not explicitly include spousal rape<sup id="cite_ref-192" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-192">[law 47]</a></sup> and it is not recognised by customary law.<sup id="cite_ref-sexualrightsdatabase_Fiji_190-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sexualrightsdatabase_Fiji-190">[144]</a></sup> However, in Dutt v The State [2006], the court ruled that spousal rape is a crime under the rape law.<sup id="cite_ref-sexualrightsdatabase_Fiji_190-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sexualrightsdatabase_Fiji-190">[144]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Finland" title="Finland">Finland</a> </td>
