         <td style="background:#9F9;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-yes">Yes<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesfinland2017_Finland]_193-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesfinland2017_Finland]-193">[146]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>The law criminalises rape, including spousal rape, and the government enforced the law effectively. Rape is punishable by up to four years’ imprisonment. If the offender used violence, the offense is considered aggravated, and the penalty may be more severe.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124452httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017eur277163htm_Finland]_194-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124452httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017eur277163htm_Finland]-194">[147]</a></sup> Marital rape was criminalised in 1994.<sup id="cite_ref-195" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-195">[148]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a> </td> 
         <td style="background:#9F9;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-yes">Explicitly criminalised<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesfrance2017_France]_196-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesfrance2017_France]-196">[149]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>The law criminalises rape, including spousal rape, and domestic violence, and the government generally enforced the law effectively.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124454httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017eur277165htm_France]_197-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124454httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017eur277165htm_France]-197">[150]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Court_of_Cassation_(France)" title="Court of Cassation (France)">Court of Cassation</a> authorized prosecution of spouses for rape or sexual assault in 1990.<sup id="cite_ref-RJSimon20_198-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RJSimon20-198">[151]</a></sup> In 1994, Law 94-89 criminalised marital rape;<sup id="cite_ref-RJSimon20_198-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RJSimon20-198">[151]</a></sup> a second law, passed 4 April 2006, makes rape by a partner an aggravating circumstance in prosecuting rape.<sup id="cite_ref-199" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-199">[152]</a></sup> (Article 222-24(11) of the Criminal Code)<sup id="cite_ref-200" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-200">[law 48]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr>
       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="G">G</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Marital_rape_laws_by_country&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: G">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <table class="sortable wikitable"> 
       <tbody>
        <tr> 
         <th>Country </th> 
         <th>Criminalised </th> 
         <th class="unsortable">Notes </th>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Gabon" title="Gabon">Gabon</a><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesgabon2017_Gabon]_201-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesgabon2017_Gabon]-201">[153]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td style="background:#9F9;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-yes">Explicitly criminalised<sup id="cite_ref-Gabon_202-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gabon-202">[154]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>Marital rape was criminalised in 2013 and the penalties on conviction are five to ten-year imprisonment sentences and a very heavy fine.<sup id="cite_ref-Gabon_202-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gabon-202">[154]</a></sup> Authorities seldom prosecute rape cases.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124459httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017af277001htm_Gabon]_203-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124459httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017af277001htm_Gabon]-203">[155]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Gambia" class="mw-redirect" title="Gambia">Gambia</a> </td> 
         <td style="background:#9F9;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-yes">Yes<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesgambia-the2017_Gambia,_the]_204-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesgambia-the2017_Gambia,_the]-204">[156]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEThe_State_of_African_Women2018146_66-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEThe_State_of_African_Women2018146-66">[48]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>Although spousal rape was widespread;, police generally considered it a domestic issue outside its jurisdiction.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124502httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017af277003htm_Gambia,_the]_205-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124502httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017af277003htm_Gambia,_the]-205">[157]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Georgia_(country)" title="Georgia (country)">Georgia</a><sup id="cite_ref-UNIFEM-2003_61-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UNIFEM-2003-61">[45]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td style="background:#9F9;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-yes">Explicitly criminalised<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesgeorgia2017_Georgia]_206-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesgeorgia2017_Georgia]-206">[158]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>Marital rape is Explicitly criminalised by Articles 11-1 &amp; 137 of the Criminal Code<sup id="cite_ref-207" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-207">[law 49]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">Germany</a> </td> 
         <td style="background:#9F9;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-yes">Yes<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesgermany2017_Germany]_208-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesgermany2017_Germany]-208">[159]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>The law criminalises rape, including spousal rape, and provides penalties of up to 15 years in prison.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124507httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017eur277169htm_Germany]_209-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124507httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017eur277169htm_Germany]-209">[160]</a></sup> The "Marital exemption" was removed by a revised law in 1997.<sup id="cite_ref-210" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-210">[161]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Ghana" title="Ghana">Ghana</a><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEThe_State_of_African_Women2018146_66-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEThe_State_of_African_Women2018146-66">[48]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td style="background:#9F9;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-yes">Yes<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesghana2017_Ghana]_211-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesghana2017_Ghana]-211">[162]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>The "marital exemption" was removed from the country's rape laws in 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-UNSRGhana_212-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UNSRGhana-212">[163]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Greece" title="Greece">Greece</a> </td> 
         <td style="background:#9F9;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-yes">Explicitly criminalised<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesgreece2017_Greece]_213-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesgreece2017_Greece]-213">[164]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>Rape, including spousal rape, is a crime punishable by penalties ranging from five to 20 years’ imprisonment.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124512httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017eur277171htm_Greece]_214-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124512httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017eur277171htm_Greece]-214">[165]</a></sup> <i>Law 3500/2006</i>, entitled "For combating domestic violence", which punishes marital rape, entered into force on 24 October 2006.<sup id="cite_ref-215" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-215">[166]</a></sup> (Articles 1 &amp; 8)<sup id="cite_ref-216" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-216">[law 50]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Grenada" title="Grenada">Grenada</a> </td> 
         <td style="background:#9F9;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-yes">Explicitly criminalised<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesgrenada2017_Grenada]_217-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesgrenada2017_Grenada]-217">[167]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>The law criminalises rape of men or women, including spousal rape, and stipulates a sentence of flogging or up to 30 years’ imprisonment for a conviction of any nonconsensual form of sex.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124517httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017wha277333htm_Grenada]_218-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124517httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017wha277333htm_Grenada]-218">[168]</a></sup> Marital rape was criminalised in a 2012 amendment to the Criminal Code.<sup id="cite_ref-219" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-219">[169]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Guatemala" title="Guatemala">Guatemala</a> </td> 
         <td style="background:#9F9;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-yes">Explicitly criminalised<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesguatemala2017_Guatemala]_220-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesguatemala2017_Guatemala]-220">[170]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>The law criminalises rape of men or women, including spousal rape, and sets penalties between five and 50 years in prison. Police had minimal training or capacity to investigate sexual crimes or assist survivors of such crimes, and the government did not enforce the law effectively.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124521httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017wha277335htm_Guatemala]_221-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124521httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017wha277335htm_Guatemala]-221">[171]</a></sup> Spousal rape was criminalised in 2009 by Articles 28 &amp; 30 of Ley Contra la Violencia Sexual, Explotación y Trata de Personas (Law against Sexual Violence, Exploitation and Trafficking in Persons).<sup id="cite_ref-222" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-222">[law 51]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Guinea" title="Guinea">Guinea</a> </td> 
         <td style="background:#F99;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-no">No<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEThe_State_of_African_Women2018146_66-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEThe_State_of_African_Women2018146-66">[48]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-223" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-223">[172]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>The law criminalises rape and domestic violence, but both occurred frequently, and authorities rarely prosecuted perpetrators. The law does not address spousal rape.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124529httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017af277007htm_Guinea]_224-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124529httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017af277007htm_Guinea]-224">[173]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Guinea-Bissau" title="Guinea-Bissau">Guinea-Bissau</a> </td> 
         <td style="background:#9F9;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-yes">Explicitly criminalised<sup id="cite_ref-uneca_africa_225-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-uneca_africa-225">[174]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>The law prohibits rape, including spousal rape, and provides penalties for conviction of two to 12 years in prison; however, the government did not effectively enforce the law.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124531httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017af277009htm_Guinea-Bissau]_226-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124531httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017af277009htm_Guinea-Bissau]-226">[175]</a></sup> Spousal rape was criminalised in 2014 by Arts. 4(f) &amp; 25 of Law No. 6/2014.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesguinea-bissau2017_Guinea-Bissau]_227-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesguinea-bissau2017_Guinea-Bissau]-227">[176]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Guyana" title="Guyana">Guyana</a><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124535httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017wha277337htm_Guyana]_228-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124535httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017wha277337htm_Guyana]-228">[177]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td style="background:#9F9;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-yes">Explicitly criminalised<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesguyana2017_Guyana]_229-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesguyana2017_Guyana]-229">[178]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>Marital rape was criminalised by §3 &amp; 7 the Sexual Offenses Act 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-230" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-230">[179]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-231" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-231">[law 52]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="H">H</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Marital_rape_laws_by_country&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: H">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <table class="sortable wikitable"> 
       <tbody>
        <tr> 
         <th>Country </th> 
         <th>Criminalised </th> 
         <th class="unsortable">Notes </th>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Haiti" title="Haiti">Haiti</a><sup id="cite_ref-232" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-232">[180]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td style="background:#F99;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-no">No </td> 
         <td>While the law prohibits rape of men or women, it does not recognize spousal rape as a crime.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124538httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017wha277339htm_Haiti]_233-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124538httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017wha277339htm_Haiti]-233">[181]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Honduras" title="Honduras">Honduras</a> </td> 
         <td style="background:#9F9;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-yes">Explicitly criminalised<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomieshonduras2017_Honduras]_234-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomieshonduras2017_Honduras]-234">[182]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>The law criminalises all forms of rape of men or women, including spousal rape,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124540httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017wha277341htm_Honduras]_235-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124540httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017wha277341htm_Honduras]-235">[183]</a></sup> but unlike other rapes is not a "public crime" and thereby requires the survivors to complain for prosecution to occur.<sup id="cite_ref-236" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-236">[184]</a></sup> Marital rape was explicitly criminalised in 2005 by arts. 140 &amp; 141 of the Código Penal.<sup id="cite_ref-237" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-237">[law 53]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Hong_Kong" title="Hong Kong">Hong Kong</a> </td> 
         <td style="background:#9F9;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-yes">Explicitly criminalised<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomieshong-kong-sar-china2017_Hong_Kong]_238-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomieshong-kong-sar-china2017_Hong_Kong]-238">[185]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>Section 117(1B) of the Crimes Ordinance, introduced in 2002, states that "unlawful sexual intercourse (非法性交、非法的性交) does not exclude sexual intercourse that a man has with his wife".<sup id="cite_ref-239" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-239">[law 54]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Hungary" title="Hungary">Hungary</a> </td> 
         <td style="background:#9F9;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-yes">Explicitly criminalised<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomieshungary2017_Hungary]_240-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomieshungary2017_Hungary]-240">[186]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>Rape of men or women, including spousal rape, is illegal.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124543httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017eur277173htm_Hungary]_241-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124543httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017eur277173htm_Hungary]-241">[187]</a></sup> The "marital exemption" was dropped from law in 1997.<sup id="cite_ref-RJSimon25_242-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RJSimon25-242">[188]</a></sup> Secs.197(3)(b) and 459(14) of the Criminal Code explicitly criminalise spousal rape.<sup id="cite_ref-243" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-243">[law 55]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="I">I</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Marital_rape_laws_by_country&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: I">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <table class="sortable wikitable"> 
       <tbody>
        <tr> 
         <th>Country </th> 
         <th>Criminalised </th> 
         <th class="unsortable">Notes </th>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Iceland" title="Iceland">Iceland</a><sup id="cite_ref-UNIFEM-2003_61-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UNIFEM-2003-61">[45]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td style="background:#9F9;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-yes">Explicitly criminalised<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesiceland2017_Iceland]_244-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesiceland2017_Iceland]-244">[189]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>Art. 70 of the Almenn hegningarlög (Penal Code), introduced in 2006, makes a relationship between the perpetrator and victim an aggravating factor.<sup id="cite_ref-245" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-245">[law 56]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a> </td> 
         <td style="background:#F99;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-no">Explicitly excluded<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesindia2017_India]_246-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesindia2017_India]-246">[190]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>
          <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
           See also: <a href="/wiki/Rape_in_India#Marital_rape" title="Rape in India">Rape in India §&nbsp;Marital rape</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Violence_against_women_in_India#Marital_rape" title="Violence against women in India">Violence against women in India §&nbsp;Marital rape</a>
          </div> Section 375 of the <a href="/wiki/Indian_Penal_Code" title="Indian Penal Code">Indian Penal Code</a> (IPC) considers<sup id="cite_ref-247" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-247">[191]</a></sup> forced sex in marriages as a crime only when the wife is under the age of 16. Rape of estranged or separated wives is a criminal offence up to 7 years under a separate law.<sup id="cite_ref-248" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-248">[192]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124549httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017sca277281htm_India]_249-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124549httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017sca277281htm_India]-249">[193]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-250" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-250">[law 57]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Indonesia" title="Indonesia">Indonesia</a> </td> 
         <td style="background:#F99;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-no">Not clearly described<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesindonesia2017_Indonesia]_251-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesindonesia2017_Indonesia]-251">[194]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124552httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017eap277083htm_Indonesia]_252-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124552httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017eap277083htm_Indonesia]-252">[195]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>Art. 285 of the Penal Code includes "out of marriage" in the definition of rape,<sup id="cite_ref-253" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-253">[law 58]</a></sup> however, marital rape is considered a form of domestic violence under arts. 5, 8, 46, 47 and 53 of the <i>Law Regarding the Elimination of Violence in the Household, 2004</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-254" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-254">[law 59]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Iran" title="Iran">Iran</a><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWestmarlandGangoli2012_255-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWestmarlandGangoli2012-255">[196]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td style="background:#F99;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-no">Explicitly excluded<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesiran-islamic-rep2017_Iran]_256-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesiran-islamic-rep2017_Iran]-256">[197]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>Rape is illegal and subject to strict penalties, including death, but it remained a problem. The law considers sex within marriage consensual by definition (Penal Code art. 221)<sup id="cite_ref-257" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-257">[law 60]</a></sup> and, therefore, does not address spousal rape, including in cases of forced marriage.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124555httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017nea277241htm_Iran]_258-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124555httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017nea277241htm_Iran]-258">[198]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Iraq" title="Iraq">Iraq</a><sup id="cite_ref-259" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-259">[199]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td style="background:#F99;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-no">Explicitly excluded<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesiraq2017_Iraq]_260-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesiraq2017_Iraq]-260">[200]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>The law criminalises rape and permits a maximum sentence of life imprisonment if the victim dies.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124557httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017nea277243htm_Iraq]_261-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124557httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017nea277243htm_Iraq]-261">[201]</a></sup> Art. 393(1) of the Penal Code explicitly excludes spousal rape from the definition of rape.<sup id="cite_ref-262" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-262">[law 61]</a></sup> The law allows authorities to drop a rape case if the perpetrator marries the victim.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124557httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017nea277243htm_Iraq]_261-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124557httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017nea277243htm_Iraq]-261">[201]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Ireland" title="Ireland">Ireland</a><sup id="cite_ref-UNIFEM-2003_61-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UNIFEM-2003-61">[45]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td style="background:#9F9;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-yes">Yes<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesireland2017_Ireland]_263-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesireland2017_Ireland]-263">[202]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>The law criminalises rape, including spousal rape, and the government enforced the law. Most persons convicted received prison sentences of five to 12 years.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124602httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017eur277177htm_Ireland]_264-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124602httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017eur277177htm_Ireland]-264">[203]</a></sup> Section 5 of the Criminal Law (Rape) (Amendment) Act, 1990 removed "marital exemption" from Irish law.<sup id="cite_ref-Temkin86_32-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Temkin86-32">[23]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-265" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-265">[law 62]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">Israel</a><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesisrael2017_Israel]_266-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesisrael2017_Israel]-266">[204]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td style="background:#9F9;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-yes">Case Law<sup id="cite_ref-IntroCrim79_267-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IntroCrim79-267">[205]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-RiM284_268-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RiM284-268">[206]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>Rape, including spousal rape, is a felony punishable by 16 years in prison, or up to 20 years’ imprisonment.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124605httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017nea277245htm_Israel]_269-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124605httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017nea277245htm_Israel]-269">[207]</a></sup> The Israeli Supreme Court affirmed that marital rape is a crime in a 1980 decision, citing law based on the <a href="/wiki/Talmud" title="Talmud">Talmud</a><sup id="cite_ref-IntroCrim79_267-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IntroCrim79-267">[205]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-RiM284_268-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RiM284-268">[206]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">Italy</a> </td> 
         <td style="background:#9F9;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-yes">Explicitly criminalised<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesitaly2017_Italy]_270-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesitaly2017_Italy]-270">[208]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>The prescribed penalty for rape, including spousal rape, is five to 12 years in prison.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124610httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017eur277179htm_Italy]_271-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124610httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017eur277179htm_Italy]-271">[209]</a></sup> In 1976 in <i>Sentenza n. 12857 del 1976</i>, the Supreme Court ruled that "the spouse who compels the other spouse to carnal knowledge by violence or threats commits the crime of carnal violence" (as rape was then known).<sup id="cite_ref-272" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-272">[210]</a></sup> In 2013, art. 609-ter(5-quarter) was added to the Criminal Code which made rape by somebody in an 'affective relationship' with the victim an aggravating factor.<sup id="cite_ref-273" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-273">[law 63]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Ivory_Coast" title="Ivory Coast">Ivory Coast</a> </td> 
         <td style="background:#9F9;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-yes">Yes<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiescote-divoire2017_Côte_d'Ivoire]_274-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiescote-divoire2017_Côte_d'Ivoire]-274">[211]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>The law prohibits rape and provides for prison terms of five to 20 years for perpetrators.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124358httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017af276991htm_Cote_d'Ivoire]_275-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124358httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017af276991htm_Cote_d'Ivoire]-275">[212]</a></sup> The Penal does not specifically include spousal rape in the definition of rape.<sup id="cite_ref-276" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-276">[law 64]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr>
       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="J">J</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Marital_rape_laws_by_country&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: J">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <table class="sortable wikitable"> 
       <tbody>
        <tr> 
         <th>Country </th> 
         <th>Criminalised </th> 
         <th class="unsortable">Notes </th>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Jamaica" title="Jamaica">Jamaica</a><sup id="cite_ref-Postcolonial_23-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Postcolonial-23">[17]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td style="background:#F99;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-no">Explicitly excluded<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesjamaica2017_Jamaica]_277-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesjamaica2017_Jamaica]-277">[213]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>The Sexual Offences Act, Sec. 5(3)<sup id="cite_ref-278" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-278">[law 65]</a></sup> criminalises spousal rape only when spouses have separated or begun proceedings to dissolve the marriage; when the husband is under a court order not to molest or cohabit with his wife; or when the husband knows he suffers from a sexually transmitted infection.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124613httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017wha277343htm_Jamaica]_279-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124613httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017wha277343htm_Jamaica]-279">[214]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Japan" title="Japan">Japan</a> </td> 
         <td style="background:#9F9;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-yes">Yes<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesjapan2017_Japan]_280-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesjapan2017_Japan]-280">[215]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>The law criminalises all forms of rape involving force against women. The law does not deny spousal rape, but no court has ever ruled on such a case, except in situations of marital breakdown (i.e., formal or informal separation, etc.).<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124617httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017eap277085htm_Japan]_281-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124617httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017eap277085htm_Japan]-281">[216]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Jordan" title="Jordan">Jordan</a> </td> 
         <td style="background:#F99;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-no">Explicitly excluded<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesjordan2017_Jordan]_282-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesjordan2017_Jordan]-282">[217]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>The law stipulates a sentence of at least 10 years of imprisonment with hard labor for the rape of a girl or woman 15 years of age or older.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124622httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017nea277249htm_Jordan]_283-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124622httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017nea277249htm_Jordan]-283">[218]</a></sup> Art. 292(a)(1) of the Penal code explicitly excludes marital rape from the definition of rape.<sup id="cite_ref-284" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-284">[law 66]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="K">K</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Marital_rape_laws_by_country&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: K">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <table class="sortable wikitable"> 
       <tbody>
        <tr> 
         <th>Country </th> 
         <th>Criminalised </th> 
         <th class="unsortable">Notes </th>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Kazakhstan" title="Kazakhstan">Kazakhstan</a> </td> 
         <td style="background:#9F9;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-yes">Yes<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomieskazakhstan2017_Kazakhstan]_285-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomieskazakhstan2017_Kazakhstan]-285">[219]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>The law criminalises rape. The punishment for rape, including spousal rape, ranges from three to 15 years’ imprisonment.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124627httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017sca277283htm_Kazakhstan]_286-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124627httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017sca277283htm_Kazakhstan]-286">[220]</a></sup> Spousal rape is not explicitly included in the definition of rape. (Criminal Code, Art. 120)<sup id="cite_ref-287" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-287">[law 67]</a></sup> There were reports of police and judicial reluctance to act on reports of rape, particularly in spousal rape cases.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124627httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017sca277283htm_Kazakhstan]_286-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124627httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017sca277283htm_Kazakhstan]-286">[220]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Kenya" title="Kenya">Kenya</a> </td> 
         <td style="background:#9F9;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-yes">Explicitly criminalised<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEThe_State_of_African_Women2018149_155-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEThe_State_of_African_Women2018149-155">[118]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>Marital rape is excluded from the definition of rape in the Sexual Offences Act (2006), section 43(5).<sup id="cite_ref-288" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-288">[law 68]</a></sup> However it is included in Section 3(a)(vi) of the Protection Against Domestic Violence Act (2015): "‘In this Act, 'violence' means abuse that includes sexual violence within marriage".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEThe_State_of_African_Women2018149_155-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEThe_State_of_African_Women2018149-155">[118]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-289" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-289">[law 69]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Kiribati" title="Kiribati">Kiribati</a> </td> 
         <td style="background:#9F9;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-yes">Yes<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomieskiribati2017_Kiribati]_290-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomieskiribati2017_Kiribati]-290">[221]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>Rape, including spousal rape, is a crime, with a maximum penalty of life in prison, but sentences typically were much shorter.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124632httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017eap277087htm_Kiribati]_291-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124632httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017eap277087htm_Kiribati]-291">[222]</a></sup> Spousal rape is not explicitly included in the definition of rape. (Penal Code, Sec. 128)<sup id="cite_ref-292" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-292">[law 70]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Kosovo" title="Kosovo">Kosovo</a> </td> 
         <td style="background:#9F9;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-yes">Yes<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomieskosovo2017_Kosovo]_293-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomieskosovo2017_Kosovo]-293">[223]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-294" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-294">[224]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>The Kosovo Criminal Code does not explicitly include marital rape in the definition of rape. (Art. 230)<sup id="cite_ref-295" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-295">[law 71]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Kuwait" title="Kuwait">Kuwait</a><sup id="cite_ref-296" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-296">[225]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td style="background: #FFD; color: black; vertical-align: middle; text-align: center;" class="partial table-partial">Yes/No </td> 
         <td>Rape carries a maximum penalty of death, which the courts occasionally imposed for the crime though spousal rape is not covered under this law.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124647httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017nea277251htm_Kuwait]_297-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124647httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017nea277251htm_Kuwait]-297">[226]</a></sup> However, in August 2020, Kuwait passed a law passed a domestic violence law criminalizing "physical, psychological, sexual or financial mistreatment, whether in words or actions" amongst family members including spousal mistreatment. The law does not address marital rape specifically and will only fully come into effect by January 2021.<sup id="cite_ref-298" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-298">[227]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Kyrgyzstan" title="Kyrgyzstan">Kyrgyzstan</a> </td> 
         <td style="background:#9F9;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-yes">Yes<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomieskyrgyz-republic2017_Kyrgyz_Republic]_299-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomieskyrgyz-republic2017_Kyrgyz_Republic]-299">[228]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>Rape, including spousal rape, is illegal, but the government failed to enforce the law effectively. Police generally regarded spousal rape as an administrative, rather than a criminal, offense.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124650httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017sca277285htm_Kyrgyz_Republic]_300-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124650httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017sca277285htm_Kyrgyz_Republic]-300">[229]</a></sup> The Penal Code does not explicitly include marital rape in the definition of rape. (Art. 129)<sup id="cite_ref-301" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-301">[law 72]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr>
       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="L">L</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Marital_rape_laws_by_country&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: L">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <table class="sortable wikitable"> 
       <tbody>
        <tr> 
         <th>Country </th> 
         <th>Criminalised </th> 
         <th class="unsortable">Notes </th>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Laos" title="Laos">Laos</a> </td> 
         <td style="background:#9F9;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-yes">Explicitly criminalised<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomieslao-pdr2017_Lao_PDR]_302-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomieslao-pdr2017_Lao_PDR]-302">[230]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>Mrital rape was explicitly criminalised in December 2014 by art. 79 of The Law on Preventing and Combating Violence Against Women and Children.<sup id="cite_ref-303" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-303">[law 73]</a></sup> Domestic violence often went unreported due to social stigma.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124653httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017eap277093htm_Laos]_304-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124653httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017eap277093htm_Laos]-304">[231]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Latvia" title="Latvia">Latvia</a> </td> 
         <td style="background:#9F9;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-yes">Explicitly criminalised<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomieslatvia2017_Latvia]_305-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomieslatvia2017_Latvia]-305">[232]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>Spousal rape is explicitly considered rape with “aggravated circumstances.”<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124655httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017eur277183htm_Latvia]_306-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124655httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017eur277183htm_Latvia]-306">[233]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Analytical_study_16-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Analytical_study-16">[12]</a></sup> (Criminal Law, Secs. 48(1)(15) and 159)<sup id="cite_ref-307" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-307">[law 74]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Lebanon" title="Lebanon">Lebanon</a> </td> 
         <td style="background: #FFD; color: black; vertical-align: middle; text-align: center;" class="partial table-partial">Yes/No </td> 
         <td>Article 503 of the Penal Code defines rape as “forced sexual intercourse [against someone] who is not his wife by violence or threat.”<sup id="cite_ref-Lebanon_308-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lebanon-308">[law 75]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-HRW-Lebanon_309-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HRW-Lebanon-309">[234]</a></sup> Law no. 293 (2014) gives a legal “marital right of intercourse.”<sup id="cite_ref-Lebanon_308-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lebanon-308">[law 75]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-310" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-310">[235]</a></sup> However, in May 2014 the Protection of Women and Other Family Members from Domestic Violence Law added new offences of the use of threats or violence to claim the “marital right to intercourse.”<sup id="cite_ref-HRW-Lebanon_309-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HRW-Lebanon-309">[234]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-311" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-311">[236]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124658httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017nea277253htm_Lebanon]_312-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124658httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017nea277253htm_Lebanon]-312">[237]</a></sup> Critics of the law point out that the threats or violence are the criminal offences but not the rape.<sup id="cite_ref-313" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-313">[238]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Lesotho" title="Lesotho">Lesotho</a><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEThe_State_of_African_Women2018157_80-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEThe_State_of_African_Women2018157-80">[58]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td style="background:#9F9;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-yes">Explicitly criminalised<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomieslesotho2017_Lesotho]_314-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomieslesotho2017_Lesotho]-314">[239]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>The law criminalises the rape of women or men, including spousal rape (Penal Code Act, 2010, Sec. 52(2)(h)(ii)),<sup id="cite_ref-315" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-315">[law 76]</a></sup> and domestic violence. Rape convictions carry a minimum sentence of 10 years’ imprisonment.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124704httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017af277013htm_Lesotho]_316-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124704httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017af277013htm_Lesotho]-316">[240]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Liberia" title="Liberia">Liberia</a> </td> 
         <td style="background:#9F9;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-yes">Yes<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesliberia2017_Liberia]_317-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesliberia2017_Liberia]-317">[241]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>Rape is illegal, but the government did not enforce the law effectively, and rape remained a serious and pervasive problem. The law's definition of rape does not specifically criminalise spousal rape,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124707httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017af277015htm_Liberia]_318-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124707httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017af277015htm_Liberia]-318">[242]</a></sup> but "marital exemption" was removed from the law in 2006<sup id="cite_ref-Liberia-OR_319-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Liberia-OR-319">[243]</a></sup> by the Rape Amendment Act.<sup id="cite_ref-320" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-320">[law 77]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Libya" title="Libya">Libya</a> </td> 
         <td style="background:#F99;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-no">No<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEThe_State_of_African_Women2018160_12-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEThe_State_of_African_Women2018160-12">[9]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>The law criminalises rape but does not address spousal rape.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124711httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017nea277255htm_Libya]_321-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124711httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017nea277255htm_Libya]-321">[244]</a></sup> Spousal rape is not considered a crime<sup id="cite_ref-322" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-322">[245]</a></sup> but a private matter.<sup id="cite_ref-323" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-323">[246]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Liechtenstein" title="Liechtenstein">Liechtenstein</a><sup id="cite_ref-UNIFEM-2003_61-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UNIFEM-2003-61">[45]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td style="background:#9F9;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-yes">Explicitly criminalised<sup id="cite_ref-UN_Liechtenstein_324-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UN_Liechtenstein-324">[247]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>Rape, including spousal rape, is a criminal offense. Penalties for rape and sexual violence vary between one and 15 years’ imprisonment, depending on the degree of violence and humiliation of the victim, and between 10 years’ and lifetime imprisonment if the victim is killed.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124715httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017eur277185htm_Liechtenstein]_325-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124715httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017eur277185htm_Liechtenstein]-325">[248]</a></sup> Marital rape was criminalised in 2001,<sup id="cite_ref-326" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-326">[249]</a></sup> by the Law on Sexual Offenses.<sup id="cite_ref-UN_Liechtenstein_324-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UN_Liechtenstein-324">[247]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Lithuania" title="Lithuania">Lithuania</a> </td> 
         <td style="background:#9F9;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-yes">Yes<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomieslithuania2017_Lithuania]_327-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomieslithuania2017_Lithuania]-327">[250]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>Rape and domestic violence are criminal offenses, and although no law specifically criminalises spousal rape,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124718httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017eur277187htm_Lithuania]_328-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124718httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017eur277187htm_Lithuania]-328">[251]</a></sup> a wife can file a complaint against her husband for rape or sexual assault under Article 149 of the Criminal Code.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomieslithuania2017_Lithuania]_327-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomieslithuania2017_Lithuania]-327">[250]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-329" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-329">[law 78]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Luxembourg" title="Luxembourg">Luxembourg</a> </td> 
         <td style="background:#9F9;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-yes">Explicitly criminalised<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesluxembourg2017_Luxembourg]_330-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesluxembourg2017_Luxembourg]-330">[252]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>The law prohibits rape, including spousal rape, and the government enforced the law effectively. Penalties for violations range from five to 10 years’ imprisonment.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124721httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017eur277189htm_Luxembourg]_331-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124721httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017eur277189htm_Luxembourg]-331">[253]</a></sup> In 1994, in Judgment no. 223/94 V, 1994, the Court of Appeal confirmed the applicability of the provisions of the Criminal Code regarding rape to marital rape.<sup id="cite_ref-coe.int_60-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-coe.int-60">[44]</a></sup> Since 2013, the maximum penalty for rape can be doubled id carried out by a spouse (Code Pénal, Art. 377(5)).<sup id="cite_ref-332" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-332">[law 79]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr>
       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="M">M</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Marital_rape_laws_by_country&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: M">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <table class="sortable wikitable"> 
       <tbody>
        <tr> 
         <th>Country </th> 
         <th>Criminalised </th> 
         <th class="unsortable">Notes </th>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Macau" title="Macau">Macau</a> </td> 
         <td>Yes </td> 
         <td><sup id="cite_ref-333" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-333">[254]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Macedonia" class="mw-redirect" title="Republic of Macedonia">Macedonia</a> </td> 
         <td style="background:#9F9;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-yes">Yes<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesmacedonia-fyr2017_Macedonia,_FYR]_334-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesmacedonia-fyr2017_Macedonia,_FYR]-334">[255]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>The penalties for rape, including spousal rape, range from one to 15 years’ imprisonment.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124724httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017eur277191htm_Macedonia]_335-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124724httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017eur277191htm_Macedonia]-335">[256]</a></sup> Marital rape was criminalised in 1996,<sup id="cite_ref-336" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-336">[257]</a></sup> although not explicitly (Criminal Code, Art. 186).<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesmacedonia-fyr2017_Macedonia,_FYR]_334-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesmacedonia-fyr2017_Macedonia,_FYR]-334">[255]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-337" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-337">[law 80]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Madagascar" title="Madagascar">Madagascar</a><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEThe_State_of_African_Women2018157_80-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEThe_State_of_African_Women2018157-80">[58]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td style="background:#F99;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-no">Customary law<sup id="cite_ref-The_State_of_African_Women_82-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_State_of_African_Women-82">[60]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>The law prohibits rape but does not address spousal rape.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124726httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017af277017htm_Madagascar]_338-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124726httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017af277017htm_Madagascar]-338">[258]</a></sup> A bill to prohibit spousal rape was defeated in the <a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_Madagascar" title="Parliament of Madagascar">Parliament of Madagascar</a> in 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-339" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-339">[259]</a></sup> Customary law holds that sex within marriage is consensual.<sup id="cite_ref-The_State_of_African_Women_82-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_State_of_African_Women-82">[60]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Malawi" title="Malawi">Malawi</a><sup id="cite_ref-Stefiszyn_81-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Stefiszyn-81">[59]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesmalawi2017_Malawi]_340-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesmalawi2017_Malawi]-340">[260]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td style="background:#F99;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-no">Case law<sup id="cite_ref-srdb_malawi_341-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-srdb_malawi-341">[261]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>Although the definition of rape in the Penal Code (s.132) does not include a "marital exemption",<sup id="cite_ref-342" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-342">[law 81]</a></sup> the presumption of a wife's consent under Customary Law was upheld by the High Court of Malawi in R.vs. Mwasomola, 4 ALR(Mal) 572.<sup id="cite_ref-srdb_malawi_341-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-srdb_malawi-341">[261]</a></sup> The Marriage, Divorce, and Family Relations Act enacted in 2015 explicitly introduces the concept of spousal rape, but the act does not prescribe specific penalties and applies only to legally separated spouses.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124729httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017af277019htm_Malawi]_343-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124729httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017af277019htm_Malawi]-343">[262]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-344" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-344">[law 82]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Malaysia" title="Malaysia">Malaysia</a><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesmalaysia2017_Malaysia]_345-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesmalaysia2017_Malaysia]-345">[263]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td style="background: #FFD; color: black; vertical-align: middle; text-align: center;" class="partial table-partial">Yes/No </td> 
         <td>The concept of rape within marriage is not recognised. However, if a man "causes hurt or fear of death or hurt to his wife or any other person in order to have sexual intercourse with his wife ", he may be imprisoned up to five years if convicted according to Section 375A of the Penal Code (adopted on 7 September 2007).<sup id="cite_ref-346" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-346">[264]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-347" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-347">[265]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-348" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-348">[266]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-349" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-349">[law 83]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Maldives" title="Maldives">Maldives</a> </td> 
         <td style="background:#F99;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-no">Explicitly excluded<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesmaldives2017_Maldives]_350-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesmaldives2017_Maldives]-350">[267]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>The Sexual Offences Act (Act 17/2014) excludes marital rape, except in very narrow circumstances such as the couple are legally separated or one has a <a href="/wiki/Sexually_transmitted_infection" title="Sexually transmitted infection">STI</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-351" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-351">[268]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-352" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-352">[269]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Mali" title="Mali">Mali</a> </td> 
         <td style="background:#9F9;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-yes">Yes<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesmali2017_Mali]_353-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesmali2017_Mali]-353">[270]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>The Code Pénal, Art. 226, does not specifically prohibit spousal rape,<sup id="cite_ref-354" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-354">[law 84]</a></sup> but law enforcement officials stated criminal laws against rape apply to spousal rape.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124738httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017af277021htm_Mali]_355-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124738httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017af277021htm_Mali]-355">[271]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Malta" title="Malta">Malta</a> </td> 
         <td style="background:#9F9;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-yes">Explicitly criminalised<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesmalta2017_Malta]_356-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesmalta2017_Malta]-356">[272]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>The 2005 Law To Make Special Provisions For Domestic Violence<sup id="cite_ref-357" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-357">[law 85]</a></sup> added article 202(h) to the Criminal Code. This article made rape by a spouse an aggravating factor.<sup id="cite_ref-358" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-358">[law 86]</a></sup> In 2018 ACT No. XIII further changed art. 202(h), changing "spouse" to "he current or former spouse, civil union partner or cohabitant".<sup id="cite_ref-359" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-359">[law 87]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Marshall_Islands" title="Marshall Islands">Marshall Islands</a> </td> 
         <td style="background:#9F9;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-yes">Yes<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesmarshall-islands2017_Marshall_Islands]_360-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesmarshall-islands2017_Marshall_Islands]-360">[273]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>The law criminalises rape, including spousal rape, although not explicitly (Criminal Code s. 213.1(1)(a) &amp; 213.2(1)(a)),<sup id="cite_ref-361" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-361">[law 88]</a></sup> and establishes penalties of up to 25 years’ imprisonment for first-degree sexual assault.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124745httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017eap277097htm_Marshall_Islands]_362-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124745httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017eap277097htm_Marshall_Islands]-362">[274]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Mauritania" title="Mauritania">Mauritania</a> </td> 
         <td style="background:#9F9;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-yes">Yes<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesmauritania2017_Mauritania]_363-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesmauritania2017_Mauritania]-363">[275]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>Rape, including spousal rape, is illegal. Rapists who are single men face penalties of forced labor and whipping, and married rapists are subject to the death penalty.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124748httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017af277023htm_Mauritania]_364-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124748httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017af277023htm_Mauritania]-364">[276]</a></sup> The Law does not differentiate between rape within marriage and rape outside marriage.<sup id="cite_ref-365" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-365">[277]</a></sup> (Code Pénal, art. 309)<sup id="cite_ref-366" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-366">[law 89]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Mauritius" title="Mauritius">Mauritius</a> </td> 
         <td style="background:#9F9;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-yes">Explicitly criminalised<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesmauritius2017_Mauritius]_367-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesmauritius2017_Mauritius]-367">[278]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>Amendments to the Protection from Domestic Violence Act (PDVA) came into force in September 2016. The amendments redefine the term “spouse” to include unmarried couples of the opposite sex; redefine “domestic violence” to include verbal, psychological, economic, and sexual abuses. Although the amendments do not mention spousal rape, section 2.d. stipulates that a spouse cannot force or threaten the other partner into a sexual act “from which the spouse or the other person has the right to abstain.”<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124751httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017af277025htm_Mauritius]_368-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124751httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017af277025htm_Mauritius]-368">[279]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-369" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-369">[law 90]</a></sup> Spousal rape was first criminalised in 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-ExpressMauritius_370-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ExpressMauritius-370">[280]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Mexico" title="Mexico">Mexico</a> </td> 
         <td style="background:#9F9;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-yes">Explicitly criminalised<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesmexico2017_Mexico]_371-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesmexico2017_Mexico]-371">[281]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>Federal law criminalises rape of men or women and conviction carries penalties of up to 20 years’ imprisonment. Twenty-four states have laws criminalising spousal rape.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124754httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017wha277345htm_Mexico]_372-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124754httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017wha277345htm_Mexico]-372">[282]</a></sup> Article 265 bis of the Código Penal Federal explicitly criminalises rape of a "wife or concubine".<sup id="cite_ref-373" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-373">[law 91]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Federated_States_of_Micronesia" title="Federated States of Micronesia">Micronesia</a> </td> 
         <td style="background: #FFD; color: black; vertical-align: middle; text-align: center;" class="partial table-partial">Yes/No </td> 
         <td>Marital rape is explicitly excluded from the definition of rape in <a href="/wiki/Pohnpei_State" title="Pohnpei State">Pohnpei State</a> (Pohnpei Code, Title 61, Ch. 5, §5-141(2)),<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesmicronesia-fed-sts2017_Micronesia,_Fed._Sts.]_374-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesmicronesia-fed-sts2017_Micronesia,_Fed._Sts.]-374">[283]</a></sup> but not in the states of <a href="/wiki/Kosrae_State" class="mw-redirect" title="Kosrae State">Kosrae</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yap_State" title="Yap State">Yap</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chuuk_State" title="Chuuk State">Chuuk</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-375" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-375">[284]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Moldova" title="Moldova">Moldova</a> </td> 
         <td style="background:#9F9;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-yes">Explicitly criminalised<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesmoldova2017_Moldova]_376-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesmoldova2017_Moldova]-376">[285]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>The law criminalises rape or forcible sexual assault and establishes penalties for violations ranging from three years to life in prison.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124759httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017eur277195htm_Moldova]_377-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124759httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017eur277195htm_Moldova]-377">[286]</a></sup> Since 2010, the law has also explicitly criminalised spousal rape (Criminal Code, arts.133(1) &amp; 171 (2)(b2))<sup id="cite_ref-378" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-378">[law 92]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Monaco" title="Monaco">Monaco</a> </td> 
         <td style="background:#9F9;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-yes">Explicitly criminalised </td> 
         <td>Rape, including spousal rape, is a criminal offense with penalties of five, 10, and up to 20 years in prison, depending on the type of offense.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124802httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017eur277197htm_Monaco]_379-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124802httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017eur277197htm_Monaco]-379">[287]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Analytical_study_16-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Analytical_study-16">[12]</a></sup> Spousal rape was explicitly criminalised Law No. 1.382 of 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-380" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-380">[288]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Mongolia" title="Mongolia">Mongolia</a> </td> 
         <td style="background:#9F9;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-yes">Explicitly criminalised<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesmongolia2017_Mongolia]_381-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesmongolia2017_Mongolia]-381">[289]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>The criminal code outlaws sexual intercourse through physical violence, or threat of violence, and provides for sentences of one to 20 years’ imprisonment or life imprisonment, depending on the circumstances.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124805httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017eap277101htm_Mongolia]_382-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124805httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017eap277101htm_Mongolia]-382">[290]</a></sup> Marital rape was criminalised by the Law to Combat Domestic Violence (art. 6.1.4).<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesmongolia2017_Mongolia]_381-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesmongolia2017_Mongolia]-381">[289]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Montenegro" title="Montenegro">Montenegro</a> </td> 
         <td style="background:#9F9;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-yes">Yes<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesmontenegro2017_Montenegro]_383-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesmontenegro2017_Montenegro]-383">[291]</a></sup> </td>
