         <td>In most cases the penalty provided by law for rape, including spousal rape, is one to 10 years in prison. In practice, the average conviction resulted in 3 years.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124808httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017eur277199htm_Montenegro]_384-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124808httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017eur277199htm_Montenegro]-384">[292]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Analytical_study_16-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Analytical_study-16">[12]</a></sup> Spousal rape is not explicitly included in the definition of rape (Criminal Code, art. 204).<sup id="cite_ref-385" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-385">[law 93]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Morocco" title="Morocco">Morocco</a> </td> 
         <td style="background:#F99;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-no">No<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEThe_State_of_African_Women2018160_12-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEThe_State_of_African_Women2018160-12">[9]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>Spousal rape is not a crime.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124811httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017nea277257htm_Morocco]_386-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124811httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017nea277257htm_Morocco]-386">[293]</a></sup> "Hakkaoui Law" (named after Minister for Family Affairs and Women's Issues, <a href="/wiki/Bassima_Hakkaoui" title="Bassima Hakkaoui">Bassima Hakkaoui</a>, criminalising violence against women has came into force in September 2018 but failed to address marital rape.<sup id="cite_ref-387" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-387">[294]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-388" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-388">[295]</a></sup> In March 2013, the Moroccan Minister of Justice stated that marital rape couldn't be criminalised: “you can't deprive a man of what is rightfully his."<sup id="cite_ref-389" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-389">[296]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Mozambique" title="Mozambique">Mozambique</a> </td> 
         <td style="background:#9F9;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-yes">Explicitly criminalised<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesmozambique2017_Mozambique]_390-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesmozambique2017_Mozambique]-390">[297]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-SADC_19-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SADC-19">[14]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>The law criminalises rape, including spousal rape, and domestic violence. Penalties for conviction range from two to eight years’ imprisonment if the victim is 12 years of age or older and 20 to 24 years’ imprisonment if the victim is under 12.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124818httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017af277027htm_Mozambique]_391-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124818httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017af277027htm_Mozambique]-391">[298]</a></sup> Marital rape is explicitly criminalised by Law N.29/2009 on Domestic Violence Perpetrated Against Women, (arts. 3 &amp; 17)<sup id="cite_ref-392" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-392">[law 94]</a></sup> and the Criminal Code Law N.35/2014, (arts. 37(aa) &amp; 218).<sup id="cite_ref-393" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-393">[law 95]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Myanmar" title="Myanmar">Myanmar</a> </td> 
         <td style="background:#F99;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-no">Explicitly excluded<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesmyanmar2017_Myanmar]_394-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesmyanmar2017_Myanmar]-394">[299]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>Spousal rape is not a crime unless the wife is younger than 13 years,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124308httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017eap277069htm_Burma]_395-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124308httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017eap277069htm_Burma]-395">[300]</a></sup> and is explicitly excluded from the definition of rape in section 375 of the Penal Code.<sup id="cite_ref-396" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-396">[law 96]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr>
       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="N">N</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Marital_rape_laws_by_country&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: N">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <table class="sortable wikitable"> 
       <tbody>
        <tr> 
         <th>Country </th> 
         <th>Criminalised </th> 
         <th class="unsortable">Notes </th>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Namibia" title="Namibia">Namibia</a> </td> 
         <td style="background:#9F9;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-yes">Explicitly criminalised<sup id="cite_ref-The_State_of_African_Women_82-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_State_of_African_Women-82">[60]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-uneca_africa_225-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-uneca_africa-225">[174]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesnamibia2017_Namibia]_397-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesnamibia2017_Namibia]-397">[301]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>The law criminalises rape of men and women, including spousal rape. By law rape is defined as the commitment of any sexual act under coercive circumstances. The courts tried numerous cases of rape during the year, and the government generally enforced court sentences providing between five and 45 years’ imprisonment for those convicted.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124825httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017af277029htm_Namibia]_398-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124825httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017af277029htm_Namibia]-398">[302]</a></sup> Marital rape was outlawed in 2000,<sup id="cite_ref-399" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-399">[303]</a></sup> by section 2(3) of the Combating of Rape Act.<sup id="cite_ref-400" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-400">[law 97]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Nauru" title="Nauru">Nauru</a> </td> 
         <td style="background:#9F9;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-yes">Explicitly criminalised<sup id="cite_ref-401" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-401">[304]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>Rape is a crime and carries a maximum penalty of 25 years’ imprisonment. Section 104 of the 2016 Crimes Act<sup id="cite_ref-402" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-402">[law 98]</a></sup> specifically applies penalties for rape of married and de facto partners.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124834httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017eap277103htm_Nauru]_403-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124834httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017eap277103htm_Nauru]-403">[305]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Nepal" title="Nepal">Nepal</a> </td> 
         <td style="background:#9F9;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-yes">Explicitly criminalised<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesnepal2017_Nepal]_404-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesnepal2017_Nepal]-404">[306]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>Section 219 (4) of the 2017 Criminal Code Bill states, “If a man rapes his wife when he is still in marital relationship with her, he shall be sentenced to up to five years in jail.”.<sup id="cite_ref-405" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-405">[307]</a></sup> Marital rape was also criminalised under the previous Criminal Code (2006).<sup id="cite_ref-UNIFEM-2003_61-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UNIFEM-2003-61">[45]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Netherlands" title="Netherlands">Netherlands</a> </td> 
         <td style="background:#9F9;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-yes">Yes<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesnetherlands2017_Netherlands]_406-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesnetherlands2017_Netherlands]-406">[308]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>The law in all parts of the kingdom criminalises rape, including spousal rape, and domestic violence. The penalty is imprisonment not exceeding 12 years, a fine not exceeding 78 thousand euros ($93,600), or both. In case of violence against a spouse, the penalty for various forms of abuse can be increased by one-third.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124841httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017eur277201htm_Netherlands]_407-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124841httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017eur277201htm_Netherlands]-407">[309]</a></sup> Legislative changes provided a new definition for rape in 1991, which removed the marital exemption, and also made the crime gender-neutral.<sup id="cite_ref-408" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-408">[310]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/New_Zealand" title="New Zealand">New Zealand</a> </td> 
         <td style="background:#9F9;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-yes">Explicitly criminalised<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesnew-zealand2017_New_Zealand]_409-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesnew-zealand2017_New_Zealand]-409">[311]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>The law criminalises rape, including spousal rape (Crimes Act 1961, sec. 128(4)).<sup id="cite_ref-410" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-410">[law 99]</a></sup> The maximum penalty is 20 years’ imprisonment.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124846httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017eap277105htm_New_Zealand]_411-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124846httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017eap277105htm_New_Zealand]-411">[312]</a></sup> Marital rape was first criminalised in 1985.<sup id="cite_ref-Temkin86_32-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Temkin86-32">[23]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Nicaragua" title="Nicaragua">Nicaragua</a> </td> 
         <td style="background:#9F9;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-yes">Explicitly criminalised<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesnicaragua2017_Nicaragua]_412-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesnicaragua2017_Nicaragua]-412">[313]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>The law criminalises all forms of rape of men or women, regardless of the relationship between the victim and the accused. Sentences for those convicted of rape range from eight to 12 years’ imprisonment.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124849httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017wha277347htm_Nicaragua]_413-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124849httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017wha277347htm_Nicaragua]-413">[314]</a></sup> Marital rape was criminalised in 2012 by Ley No. 779<sup id="cite_ref-414" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-414">[law 100]</a></sup> which modified arts. 37 &amp; 169 of the Código Penal.<sup id="cite_ref-415" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-415">[law 101]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Niger" title="Niger">Niger</a> </td> 
         <td style="background:#9F9;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-yes">Yes<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesniger2017_Niger]_416-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesniger2017_Niger]-416">[315]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>The law does not explicitly recognize spousal rape,<sup id="cite_ref-417" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-417">[law 102]</a></sup> and authorities seldom prosecuted it. Victims often sought to deal with the rape within the family or were pressured to do so, and many victims did not report spousal rape due to fear of retribution, including loss of economic support.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124852httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017af277031htm_Niger]_418-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124852httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017af277031htm_Niger]-418">[316]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Nigeria" title="Nigeria">Nigeria</a> </td> 
         <td style="background:#F99;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-no">Explicitly excluded<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEThe_State_of_African_Women2018146_66-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEThe_State_of_African_Women2018146-66">[48]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesnigeria2017_Nigeria]_419-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesnigeria2017_Nigeria]-419">[317]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>Marital rape is explicitly excluded from the definition of rape in the Penal Code provided the spouse has reached puberty (Article 282(2)).<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEThe_State_of_African_Women2018146_66-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEThe_State_of_African_Women2018146-66">[48]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/North_Korea" title="North Korea">North Korea</a> </td> 
         <td style="background:#F99;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-no">No<sup id="cite_ref-420" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-420">[318]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>As of 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-421" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-421">[319]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Norway" title="Norway">Norway</a> </td> 
         <td style="background:#9F9;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-yes">Yes<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesnorway2017_Norway]_422-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesnorway2017_Norway]-422">[320]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>The law criminalises rape, including spousal rape,<sup id="cite_ref-423" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-423">[law 103]</a></sup> and the government generally enforced the law. The penalty for rape is up to 21 years in prison, depending on the severity of the assault, the age of the victim, and the circumstances in which the crime occurred.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124857httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017eur277203htm_Norway]_424-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124857httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017eur277203htm_Norway]-424">[321]</a></sup> The "marital exemption" was removed from the law in 1971.<sup id="cite_ref-Kenyan_Woman_177-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kenyan_Woman-177">[134]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr>
       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="O">O</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Marital_rape_laws_by_country&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: O">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <table class="sortable wikitable"> 
       <tbody>
        <tr> 
         <th>Country </th> 
         <th>Criminalised </th> 
         <th class="unsortable">Notes </th>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Oman" title="Oman">Oman</a> </td> 
         <td style="background:#F99;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-no">Explicitly excluded<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesoman2017_Oman]_425-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesoman2017_Oman]-425">[322]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>The law criminalises rape with penalties of up to 15 years in prison but does not criminalise spousal rape.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124900httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017nea277259htm_Oman]_426-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124900httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017nea277259htm_Oman]-426">[323]</a></sup> Article 218(1) of the Penal Code of Oman explicitly excludes marital rape from the definition of rape.<sup id="cite_ref-427" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-427">[law 104]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr>
       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="P">P</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Marital_rape_laws_by_country&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: P">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <table class="sortable wikitable"> 
       <tbody>
        <tr> 
         <th>Country </th> 
         <th>Criminalised </th> 
         <th class="unsortable">Notes </th>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Pakistan" title="Pakistan">Pakistan</a> </td> 
         <td style="background: #ececec; color: #2C2C2C; font-size: smaller; vertical-align: middle; text-align: center;" class="unknown table-unknown">Unclear </td> 
         <td>The Offence of Zina (Enforcement of Hudood) Ordinance, 1979 included in its definition of rape "to whom he or she is not validly married". This ordinance was repealed by the <a href="/wiki/Women%27s_Protection_Bill" title="Women's Protection Bill">Protection of Women (Criminal Laws Amendment) Act, 2006</a> and rape was now defined in Section 375 of the Penal Code.<sup id="cite_ref-428" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-428">[law 105]</a></sup> The new definition did not include a reference to marriage. It was argued that the intent was to include marital rape in the offence.<sup id="cite_ref-Khan_429-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Khan-429">[324]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-430" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-430">[325]</a></sup> However, as of February 2015, there were no reports of a case being brought before a superior court to clarify the law.<sup id="cite_ref-Khan_429-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Khan-429">[324]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Palau" title="Palau">Palau</a> </td> 
         <td style="background:#9F9;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-yes">Yes<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiespalau2017_Palau]_431-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiespalau2017_Palau]-431">[326]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>Rape, including spousal rape, is a crime punishable by a maximum 25 years’ imprisonment, a fine of $50,000 (national currency is U.S. dollar), or both.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124912httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017eap277107htm_Palau]_432-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124912httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017eap277107htm_Palau]-432">[327]</a></sup> The 2012 Palau Family Protection Act removed the "marital exemption" from Palau National Code.<sup id="cite_ref-433" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-433">[law 106]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/State_of_Palestine" title="State of Palestine">Palestine</a> </td> 
         <td style="background:#F99;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-no">Explicitly excluded<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomieswest-bank-and-gaza2017_West_Bank_and_Gaza]_434-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomieswest-bank-and-gaza2017_West_Bank_and_Gaza]-434">[328]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-435" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-435">[329]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>Article 292(1) of the Criminal Code of 1960 explicitly excludes marital rape from the law on rape.<sup id="cite_ref-436" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-436">[law 107]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Panama" title="Panama">Panama</a> </td> 
         <td style="background:#9F9;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-yes">Explicitly criminalised<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiespanama2017_Panama]_437-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiespanama2017_Panama]-437">[330]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>The law criminalises rape of men or women, including spousal rape, with prison terms of five to 10 years.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124915httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017wha277349htm_Panama]_438-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124915httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017wha277349htm_Panama]-438">[331]</a></sup> In 2013, Ley No. 82<sup id="cite_ref-439" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-439">[law 108]</a></sup> amended the Código Penal to explicitly criminalise marital rape (arts. 91 &amp; 174).<sup id="cite_ref-440" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-440">[law 109]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Papua_New_Guinea" title="Papua New Guinea">Papua New Guinea</a> </td> 
         <td style="background:#9F9;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-yes">Yes<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiespapua-new-guinea2017_Papua_New_Guinea]_441-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiespapua-new-guinea2017_Papua_New_Guinea]-441">[332]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>Rape, including spousal rape, is a crime punishable by imprisonment ranging from 15 years to life. The legal system allows village chiefs to negotiate the payment of compensation in lieu of trials for rapists.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124919httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017eap277109htm_Papua_New_Guinea]_442-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124919httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017eap277109htm_Papua_New_Guinea]-442">[333]</a></sup> In 2002, The Criminal Code (Sexual Offences and Crimes against Children) Act removed the rape "marital exemption" from the Criminal Code<sup id="cite_ref-443" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-443">[334]</a></sup> (sec 347).<sup id="cite_ref-444" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-444">[law 110]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Paraguay" title="Paraguay">Paraguay</a> </td> 
         <td style="background:#9F9;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-yes">Yes<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesparaguay2017_Paraguay]_445-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesparaguay2017_Paraguay]-445">[335]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>The law criminalises rape of men or women, including spousal rape, and provides penalties of up to 10 years in prison for rape or sexual assault.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124922httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017wha277351htm_Paraguay]_446-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124922httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017wha277351htm_Paraguay]-446">[336]</a></sup> Marital rape is not explicitly criminalised by the Código Penal (art. 128).<sup id="cite_ref-447" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-447">[law 111]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Peru" title="Peru">Peru</a> </td> 
         <td style="background:#9F9;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-yes">Explicitly criminalised<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesperu2017_Peru]_448-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesperu2017_Peru]-448">[337]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>The law criminalises rape of men or women, including spousal rape, with penalties of six to eight years in prison.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124924httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017wha277353htm_Peru]_449-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124924httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017wha277353htm_Peru]-449">[338]</a></sup> Marital rape has been explicitly criminalised since 2007 by art. 170 of the Código Penal.<sup id="cite_ref-450" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-450">[law 112]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">Philippines</a> </td> 
         <td style="background:#9F9;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-yes">Explicitly criminalised<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesphilippines2017_Philippines]_451-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesphilippines2017_Philippines]-451">[339]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>
          <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
           See also: <a href="/wiki/Rape_in_the_Philippines#Marital_rape" title="Rape in the Philippines">Rape in the Philippines §&nbsp;Marital rape</a>
          </div> <p>Rape, including spousal rape, is illegal, with penalties ranging from 12 to 40 years’ imprisonment.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124927httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017eap277111htm_Philippines]_452-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124927httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017eap277111htm_Philippines]-452">[340]</a></sup> An anti-rape law covering marital rape was passed in 1997.<sup id="cite_ref-ARROW2011_453-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ARROW2011-453">[341]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-UNIFEM-2003_61-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UNIFEM-2003-61">[45]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-454" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-454">[law 113]</a></sup> Marital rape was explicitly criminalised by the Anti- Violence Against Women and Their Children Act of 2004 (Sec. 3(B)(a),(b)).<sup id="cite_ref-455" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-455">[law 114]</a></sup> The legality of the marital rape laws was upheld by the <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_the_Philippines" title="Supreme Court of the Philippines">Supreme Court</a> in People vs Jumawan G.R. No. 187495 (2014).<sup id="cite_ref-456" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-456">[342]</a></sup> </p> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Poland" title="Poland">Poland</a> </td> 
         <td style="background:#9F9;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-yes">Yes<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiespoland2017_Poland]_457-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiespoland2017_Poland]-457">[343]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>Rape, including spousal rape, is illegal and punishable by up to 12 years in prison.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124929httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017eur277205htm_Poland]_458-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124929httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017eur277205htm_Poland]-458">[344]</a></sup> The "marital exemption" clause was dropped when the 1932 Criminal Code was introduced.<sup id="cite_ref-459" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-459">[345]</a></sup> The Penal Code does not explicitly criminalise marital rape (art. 197).<sup id="cite_ref-460" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-460">[law 115]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Portugal" title="Portugal">Portugal</a> </td> 
         <td style="background:#9F9;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-yes">Explicitly criminalised<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesportugal2017_Portugal]_461-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesportugal2017_Portugal]-461">[346]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>The law makes rape, including spousal rape, illegal, with a penalty of three to 10 years’ imprisonment.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124933httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017eur277207htm_Portugal]_462-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124933httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017eur277207htm_Portugal]-462">[347]</a></sup> The "marital exemption" was removed from the law in 1982.<sup id="cite_ref-463" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-463">[348]</a></sup> In 2007, amendments<sup id="cite_ref-464" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-464">[law 116]</a></sup> to the Penal Code arts. 152 &amp; 164), explicitly criminalised marital rape.<sup id="cite_ref-465" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-465">[law 117]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr>
       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Q">Q</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Marital_rape_laws_by_country&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Q">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <table class="sortable wikitable"> 
       <tbody>
        <tr> 
         <th>Country </th> 
         <th>Criminalised </th> 
         <th class="unsortable">Notes </th>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Qatar" title="Qatar">Qatar</a> </td> 
         <td style="background:#9F9;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-yes">Yes<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesqatar2017_Qatar]_466-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesqatar2017_Qatar]-466">[349]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>Article 279 of the Penal Code criminalises rape.<sup id="cite_ref-467" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-467">[law 118]</a></sup> Spousal rape is not explicitly criminalised, but a woman may file a complaint. The penalty for rape is life imprisonment, regardless of the age or gender of the victim.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124935httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017nea277261htm_Qatar]_468-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124935httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017nea277261htm_Qatar]-468">[350]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr>
       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="R">R</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Marital_rape_laws_by_country&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: R">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <table class="sortable wikitable"> 
       <tbody>
        <tr> 
         <th>Country </th> 
         <th>Criminalised </th> 
         <th class="unsortable">Notes </th>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Romania" title="Romania">Romania</a> </td> 
         <td style="background:#9F9;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-yes">Explicitly criminalised<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesromania2017_Romania]_469-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesromania2017_Romania]-469">[351]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>Rape, including spousal rape, is illegal. The law provides for three to 10 years’ imprisonment for rape and two to seven years’ imprisonment for sexual assault.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124938httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017eur277209htm_Romania]_470-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124938httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017eur277209htm_Romania]-470">[352]</a></sup> In 2003, marital rape was criminalised by article 4(d) of the Law on Preventing and Fighting Against Domestic Violence.<sup id="cite_ref-471" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-471">[law 119]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">Russia</a> </td> 
         <td style="background:#9F9;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-yes">Yes<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesrussian-federation2017_Russian_Federation]_472-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesrussian-federation2017_Russian_Federation]-472">[353]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>Rape is illegal, and the law provides the same punishment for a relative, including the spouse, who commits rape as for a nonrelative.<sup id="cite_ref-473" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-473">[law 120]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124944httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017eur277211htm_Russia]_474-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124944httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017eur277211htm_Russia]-474">[354]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a>, which Russia was the dominant republic, removed "marital exemption" from its rape laws in 1922.<sup id="cite_ref-475" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-475">[355]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Rwanda" title="Rwanda">Rwanda</a> </td> 
         <td style="background:#9F9;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-yes">Explicitly criminalised<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEThe_State_of_African_Women2018149_155-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEThe_State_of_African_Women2018149-155">[118]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-uneca_africa_225-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-uneca_africa-225">[174]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesrwanda2017_Rwanda]_476-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesrwanda2017_Rwanda]-476">[356]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>The law criminalises rape of men and women and spousal rape, and the government handled rape cases as a judicial priority. Penalties for conviction of spousal rape range from two months’ to life imprisonment with fines of 100,000 to 300,000 Rwandan francs.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124946httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017af277035htm_Rwanda]_477-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124946httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017af277035htm_Rwanda]-477">[357]</a></sup> Spousal rape was first criminalised in 2009,<sup id="cite_ref-AFWRRwanda_478-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AFWRRwanda-478">[358]</a></sup> when the Law on prevention and punishment of gender- based violence came into effect.<sup id="cite_ref-479" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-479">[law 121]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr>
       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="S">S</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Marital_rape_laws_by_country&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: S">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <table class="sortable wikitable"> 
       <tbody>
        <tr> 
         <th>Country </th> 
         <th>Criminalised </th> 
         <th class="unsortable">Notes </th>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Saint_Kitts_and_Nevis" title="Saint Kitts and Nevis">Saint Kitts and Nevis</a> </td> 
         <td style="background:#9F9;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-yes">Yes<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesst-kitts-and-nevis2017_St._Kitts_and_Nevis]_480-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesst-kitts-and-nevis2017_St._Kitts_and_Nevis]-480">[359]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>Marital rape is neither explicitly included or excluded from article 46 of the Offences against the Person Act which criminalises rape.<sup id="cite_ref-481" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-481">[law 122]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Saint_Lucia" title="Saint Lucia">Saint Lucia</a><sup id="cite_ref-Postcolonial_23-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Postcolonial-23">[17]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td style="background:#F99;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-no">Explicitly excluded<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesst-lucia2017_Saint_Lucia]_482-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesst-lucia2017_Saint_Lucia]-482">[360]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>Section 123(3) of the Criminal Code<sup id="cite_ref-483" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-483">[law 123]</a></sup> explicitly excludes marital rape except when a couple is divorced or separated or when there is a protection order from the Family Court.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124952httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017wha277357htm_Saint_Lucia]_484-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124952httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017wha277357htm_Saint_Lucia]-484">[361]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines" title="Saint Vincent and the Grenadines">Saint Vincent and the Grenadines</a> </td> 
         <td style="background:#9F9;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-yes">Yes<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesst-vincent-and-the-grenadines2017_St._Vincent_and_the_Grenadines]_485-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesst-vincent-and-the-grenadines2017_St._Vincent_and_the_Grenadines]-485">[362]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>Rape, including spousal rape (although not explicitly),<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesst-vincent-and-the-grenadines2017_St._Vincent_and_the_Grenadines]_485-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesst-vincent-and-the-grenadines2017_St._Vincent_and_the_Grenadines]-485">[362]</a></sup> is illegal, and the government generally enforced the law when victims came forward. Sentences for rape begin at 10 years’ imprisonment.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124955httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017wha277359htm_Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines]_486-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124955httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017wha277359htm_Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines]-486">[363]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Samoa" title="Samoa">Samoa</a> </td> 
         <td style="background:#9F9;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-yes">Explicitly criminalised<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiessamoa2017_Samoa]_487-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiessamoa2017_Samoa]-487">[364]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>The 2013 Crimes Act removed the "marital exemption" from the Crimes Ordinance 1961,<sup id="cite_ref-488" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-488">[365]</a></sup> and section 49(4) explicitly criminalised marital rape.<sup id="cite_ref-489" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-489">[law 124]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/San_Marino" title="San Marino">San Marino</a> </td> 
         <td style="background:#9F9;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-yes">Explicitly criminalised<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiessan-marino2017_San_Marino]_490-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiessan-marino2017_San_Marino]-490">[366]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>Rape, including spousal rape, is a criminal offense, and the government effectively prosecuted persons accused of such crimes. The penalty for rape is two to six years in prison.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422125001httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017eur277213htm_San_Marino]_491-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422125001httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017eur277213htm_San_Marino]-491">[367]</a></sup> Article 10 of the 2008 Prevention and Repression of Violence against Women and Gender-Based Violence Law made rape by a spouse an aggravating factor.<sup id="cite_ref-492" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-492">[law 125]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Sao_Tome_and_Principe" class="mw-redirect" title="Sao Tome and Principe">Sao Tome and Principe</a><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEThe_State_of_African_Women2018152_100-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEThe_State_of_African_Women2018152-100">[73]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td style="background:#9F9;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-yes">Explicitly criminalised<sup id="cite_ref-uneca_africa_225-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-uneca_africa-225">[174]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>Rape, including spousal rape, is illegal and punishable by two to 12 years’ imprisonment.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422125004httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017af277037htm_Sao_Tome_and_Principe]_493-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422125004httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017af277037htm_Sao_Tome_and_Principe]-493">[368]</a></sup> Marital rape was explicitly criminalised by Law No. 11/2008, Art. 15<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiessao-tome-and-principe2017_São_Tomé_and_Príncipe]_494-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiessao-tome-and-principe2017_São_Tomé_and_Príncipe]-494">[369]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Saudi_Arabia" title="Saudi Arabia">Saudi Arabia</a> </td> 
         <td style="background:#F99;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-no">No<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiessaudi-arabia2017_Saudi_Arabia]_495-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiessaudi-arabia2017_Saudi_Arabia]-495">[370]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>Rape is a criminal offense under sharia with a wide range of penalties from flogging to execution. The law does not recognize spousal rape as a crime.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422125006httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017nea277263htm_Saudi_Arabia]_496-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422125006httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017nea277263htm_Saudi_Arabia]-496">[371]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Senegal" title="Senegal">Senegal</a> </td> 
         <td style="background:#9F9;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-yes">Yes<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiessenegal2017_Senegal]_497-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiessenegal2017_Senegal]-497">[372]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>The law prohibits rape, which is punishable by five to 10 years’ imprisonment. Nevertheless, the government rarely enforced the law, and rape was widespread. The law does not address spousal rape,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422125010httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017af277039htm_Senegal]_498-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422125010httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017af277039htm_Senegal]-498">[373]</a></sup> but does not exclude it from the definition of rape in article 320 of the Criminal Code.<sup id="cite_ref-499" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-499">[law 126]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Serbia" title="Serbia">Serbia</a> </td> 
         <td style="background:#9F9;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-yes">Explicitly criminalised<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesserbia2017_Serbia]_500-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesserbia2017_Serbia]-500">[374]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>Rape, including spousal rape, is punishable by up to 40 years in prison. The government did not enforce the law effectively.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422125013httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017eur277215htm_Serbia]_501-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422125013httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017eur277215htm_Serbia]-501">[375]</a></sup> The "marital exemption" was dropped in 2002,<sup id="cite_ref-502" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-502">[376]</a></sup> and marital rape explicitly criminalised by the 2016 Law on the Prevention of Domestic Violence (arts. 3 &amp; 4(2)).<sup id="cite_ref-503" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-503">[law 127]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Seychelles" title="Seychelles">Seychelles</a> </td> 
         <td style="background:#9F9;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-yes">Yes<sup id="cite_ref-SADC_19-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SADC-19">[14]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesseychelles2017_Seychelles]_504-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesseychelles2017_Seychelles]-504">[377]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>Rape is a criminal offense under Sec. 130 of the Penal Code, for which conviction is punishable by a maximum of 20 years’ imprisonment. Marital rape is not explicitly criminalised.<sup id="cite_ref-505" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-505">[law 128]</a></sup> Nevertheless, rape was a problem, and the government did not enforce the law effectively.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422125016httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017af277041htm_Seychelles]_506-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422125016httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017af277041htm_Seychelles]-506">[378]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Sierra_Leone" title="Sierra Leone">Sierra Leone</a><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEThe_State_of_African_Women2018146_66-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEThe_State_of_African_Women2018146-66">[48]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td style="background:#9F9;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-yes">Explicitly criminalised<sup id="cite_ref-uneca_africa_225-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-uneca_africa-225">[174]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiessierra-leone2017_Sierra_Leone]_507-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiessierra-leone2017_Sierra_Leone]-507">[379]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>The law has specifically prohibited spousal rape<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422125020httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017af277043htm_Sierra_Leone]_508-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422125020httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017af277043htm_Sierra_Leone]-508">[380]</a></sup> since 2012<sup id="cite_ref-unwomen1_509-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-unwomen1-509">[381]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-510" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-510">[382]</a></sup> by Secs. 5 and 6 of the Sexual Offences Act.<sup id="cite_ref-511" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-511">[law 129]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Singapore" title="Singapore">Singapore</a> </td> 
         <td style="background:#9F9;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-yes">Yes<sup id="cite_ref-Singapore_512-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Singapore-512">[law 130]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>
          <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
           See also: <a href="/wiki/Marital_rape_immunity_in_Singapore" title="Marital rape immunity in Singapore">Marital rape immunity in Singapore</a>
          </div> Before 2020, spousal rape was explicitly excluded from rape laws except in very narrow circumstances (Sec. 375 of the Penal Code),<sup id="cite_ref-Singapore_512-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Singapore-512">[law 130]</a></sup> but husbands who force their wives to have intercourse may be prosecuted for other offenses, such as assault. Spousal rape is a criminal offense when the couple is separated, subject to an interim divorce order that has not become final, or subject to a written separation agreement, as well as when a court has issued a protection order against the husband.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422125024httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017eap277115htm_Singapore]_513-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422125024httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017eap277115htm_Singapore]-513">[383]</a></sup> This exemption was lifted on January 1, 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-514" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-514">[384]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Slovakia" title="Slovakia">Slovakia</a> </td> 
         <td style="background:#9F9;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-yes">Explicitly criminalised<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesslovak-republic2017_Slovak_Republic]_515-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesslovak-republic2017_Slovak_Republic]-515">[385]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>Sections 199 and 127(5) of the criminal code explicitly include spousal rape under the crime of rape and sexual violence.<sup id="cite_ref-516" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-516">[law 131]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Slovenia" title="Slovenia">Slovenia</a> </td> 
         <td style="background:#9F9;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-yes">Explicitly criminalised<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesslovenia2017_Slovenia]_517-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesslovenia2017_Slovenia]-517">[386]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>Marital rape is explicitly criminalised by article 170 of the Criminal Code.<sup id="cite_ref-518" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-518">[law 132]</a></sup> As a republic with <a href="/wiki/Yugoslavia" title="Yugoslavia">Yugoslavia</a>, marital rape was first criminalised by Slovenia in 1977.<sup id="cite_ref-Slovenia_519-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Slovenia-519">[387]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Solomon_Islands" title="Solomon Islands">Solomon Islands</a> </td> 
         <td style="background:#9F9;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-yes">Explicitly criminalised<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiessolomon-islands2017_Solomon_Islands]_520-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiessolomon-islands2017_Solomon_Islands]-520">[388]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>Marital rape is explicitly criminalised by section 5(136F)(2)of the Penal Code (Amendment) (Sexual Offences) Act 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-521" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-521">[law 133]</a></sup> Rape carries a maximum penalty of life imprisonment.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422125032httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017eap277117htm_Solomon_Islands]_522-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422125032httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017eap277117htm_Solomon_Islands]-522">[389]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Somalia" title="Somalia">Somalia</a><sup id="cite_ref-Fgspc_523-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fgspc-523">[390]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td style="background: #FFD; color: black; vertical-align: middle; text-align: center;" class="partial table-partial">Yes/No<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422125035httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017af277045htm_Somalia]_524-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422125035httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017af277045htm_Somalia]-524">[391]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>There are no federal laws against spousal violence, including rape, although in May 2016, the Council of Ministers approved a national gender policy that gives the government the right to sue anyone convicted of committing gender-based violence, such as the killing or rape of a woman.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422125035httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017af277045htm_Somalia]_524-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422125035httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017af277045htm_Somalia]-524">[391]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/South_Africa" title="South Africa">South Africa</a><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiessouth-africa2017_South_Africa]_525-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiessouth-africa2017_South_Africa]-525">[392]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td style="background:#9F9;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-yes">Explicitly criminalised<sup id="cite_ref-The_State_of_African_Women_82-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_State_of_African_Women-82">[60]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-uneca_africa_225-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-uneca_africa-225">[174]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>Spousal rape was criminalised in 1993<sup id="cite_ref-526" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-526">[393]</a></sup> by article 5 of the Prevention of Family Violence Act,<sup id="cite_ref-527" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-527">[law 134]</a></sup> although the first prosecution wasn't until 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-528" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-528">[394]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/South_Korea" title="South Korea">South Korea</a> </td> 
         <td style="background:#9F9;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-yes">Court decision<sup id="cite_ref-South_Korea_529-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-South_Korea-529">[395]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>Although no specific statute defines spousal rape as illegal, the <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_South_Korea" title="Supreme Court of South Korea">Supreme Court</a> acknowledged marital rape as illegal in 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-South_Korea_529-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-South_Korea-529">[395]</a></sup> The penalty for rape ranges from a minimum of three years’ to life imprisonment depending on the specific circumstances.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124638httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017eap277091htm_South_Korea]_530-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422124638httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017eap277091htm_South_Korea]-530">[396]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-WSKorea_531-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WSKorea-531">[397]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/South_Sudan" title="South Sudan">South Sudan</a><sup id="cite_ref-auto_532-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-532">[398]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiessouth-sudan2017_South_Sudan]_533-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiessouth-sudan2017_South_Sudan]-533">[399]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td style="background:#F99;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-no">Explicitly excluded<sup id="cite_ref-Kenyan_Woman_177-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kenyan_Woman-177">[134]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422125040httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017af277049htm_South_Sudan]_534-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422125040httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017af277049htm_South_Sudan]-534">[400]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>Article 247(3) of the 2008 Penal Code is explicit that marital rape is not an offence.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEThe_State_of_African_Women2018149_155-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEThe_State_of_African_Women2018149-155">[118]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-535" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-535">[law 135]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spain</a> </td> 
         <td style="background:#9F9;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-yes">Court decision<sup id="cite_ref-Spain_536-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Spain-536">[401]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>The law prohibits rape, including spousal rape, and the government generally enforced the law effectively. The penalty for rape is six to 12 years in prison.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422125044httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017eur277221htm_Spain]_537-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422125044httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017eur277221htm_Spain]-537">[402]</a></sup> The Supreme Court ruled in 1992 that sex within marriage must be consensual.<sup id="cite_ref-Spain_536-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Spain-536">[401]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Sri_Lanka" title="Sri Lanka">Sri Lanka</a><sup id="cite_ref-538" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-538">[403]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td style="background:#F99;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-no">Explicitly excluded<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiessri-lanka2017_Sri_Lanka]_539-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiessri-lanka2017_Sri_Lanka]-539">[404]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>Marital rape is excluded from the definition of rape in article 363 of the Penal Code<sup id="cite_ref-540" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-540">[law 136]</a></sup> except if the spouses are legally separated.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180421104554httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017sca277293htm_Sri_Lanka]_541-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180421104554httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017sca277293htm_Sri_Lanka]-541">[405]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Sudan" title="Sudan">Sudan</a> </td> 
         <td style="background:#9F9;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-yes">Yes<sup id="cite_ref-Sudan_2016_542-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sudan_2016-542">[406]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>In February 2015, an amendment to Article 149 of the Criminal Code changed the definition of rape. Under the new definition of rape, rape victims could no longer be prosecuted for adultery.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422125049httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017af277051htm_Sudan]_543-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422125049httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017af277051htm_Sudan]-543">[407]</a></sup> Although there is no specific prohibition of marital rape, the amendment makes it possible to prosecute marital rape.<sup id="cite_ref-Sudan_2016_542-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sudan_2016-542">[406]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Suriname" title="Suriname">Suriname</a> </td> 
         <td style="background:#9F9;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-yes">Explicitly criminalised<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiessuriname2017_Suriname]_544-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiessuriname2017_Suriname]-544">[408]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>The law criminalises rape of women, including spousal rape, and prescribes penalties for rape or forcible sexual assault of between 12 and 15 years’ imprisonment, and fines up to 100,000 Surinamese dollars.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422125051httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017wha277361htm_Suriname]_545-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422125051httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017wha277361htm_Suriname]-545">[409]</a></sup> Spousal rape was criminalised in 2009 by an amendment to the Moral Law.<sup id="cite_ref-546" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-546">[410]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-547" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-547">[law 137]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Sweden" title="Sweden">Sweden</a> </td> 
         <td style="background:#9F9;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-yes">Explicitly criminalised<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiessweden2017_Sweden]_548-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiessweden2017_Sweden]-548">[411]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>Rape, including spousal rape and domestic violence (Ch. 4, Sec. 4a of the Penal Code),<sup id="cite_ref-549" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-549">[law 138]</a></sup> are illegal, and the government enforced the law effectively. Penalties range from two to 10 years in prison.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422125059httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017eur277223htm_Sweden]_550-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422125059httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017eur277223htm_Sweden]-550">[412]</a></sup> Marital rape was first criminalised in 1965.<sup id="cite_ref-Elman_1996_90_551-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Elman_1996_90-551">[413]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Switzerland" title="Switzerland">Switzerland</a> </td> 
         <td style="background:#9F9;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-yes">Yes<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesswitzerland2017_Switzerland]_552-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesswitzerland2017_Switzerland]-552">[414]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>Rape, including spousal rape (although not explicitly so),<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesswitzerland2017_Switzerland]_552-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesswitzerland2017_Switzerland]-552">[414]</a></sup> and domestic violence, are statutory offenses for which penalties range from one to 10 years in prison (Swiss Criminal Code, art 190).<sup id="cite_ref-553" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-553">[law 139]</a></sup> The government effectively prosecuted individuals accused of such crimes.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422125101httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017eur277225htm_Switzerland]_554-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422125101httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017eur277225htm_Switzerland]-554">[415]</a></sup> The "marital exemption" was removed from law in 1992.<sup id="cite_ref-rcne_555-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rcne-555">[416]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Syria" title="Syria">Syria</a> </td> 
         <td style="background:#F99;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-no">Explicitly excluded<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiessyrian-arab-republic2017_Syrian_Arab_Republic]_556-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiessyrian-arab-republic2017_Syrian_Arab_Republic]-556">[417]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>Rape is a felony, subject to punishment by at least 15 years in prison, but the government did not enforce the law. The law further stipulates that if the rapist marries the victim, the rapist receives no punishment. The victim's family sometimes agreed to this arrangement to avoid the social stigma attached to rape.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422125104httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017nea277265htm_Syria]_557-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422125104httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017nea277265htm_Syria]-557">[418]</a></sup> Marital rape is explicitly excluded from the rape laws by art 489(1) of the Criminal Code.<sup id="cite_ref-558" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-558">[law 140]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr>
       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="T">T</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Marital_rape_laws_by_country&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: T">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <table class="sortable wikitable"> 
       <tbody>
        <tr> 
         <th>Country </th> 
         <th>Criminalised </th> 
         <th class="unsortable">Notes </th>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Republic_of_China" class="mw-redirect" title="Republic of China">Taiwan</a> </td> 
         <td style="background:#9F9;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-yes">Explicitly criminalised<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiestaiwan-china2017_Taiwan,_China]_559-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiestaiwan-china2017_Taiwan,_China]-559">[419]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>The law criminalises rape, including spousal rape, and domestic violence.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422125106httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017eap277119htm_Taiwan]_560-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422125106httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017eap277119htm_Taiwan]-560">[420]</a></sup> (Criminal Code of the Republic of China, Arts.221 and 229-1)<sup id="cite_ref-561" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-561">[law 141]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Tajikistan" title="Tajikistan">Tajikistan</a> </td> 
         <td style="background:#F99;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-no">No<sup id="cite_ref-562" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-562">[421]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>Marital rape is not recognised as a criminal offence.<sup id="cite_ref-563" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-563">[422]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Tanzania" title="Tanzania">Tanzania</a><sup id="cite_ref-564" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-564">[423]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td style="background:#F99;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-no">Explicitly excluded<sup id="cite_ref-Kenyan_Woman_177-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kenyan_Woman-177">[134]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Tanzanian_565-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tanzanian-565">[424]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>Section 5 of the 1998 Sexual Offences (Special Provisions) Act explicitly excludes marital rape<sup id="cite_ref-566" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-566">[law 142]</a></sup> on the grounds "husbands, by virtue of paying <a href="/wiki/Bride_price" title="Bride price">bride price</a>, have legal right to have unlimited sexual access to their wives”.<sup id="cite_ref-Tanzanian_565-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tanzanian-565">[424]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Thailand" title="Thailand">Thailand</a> </td> 
         <td style="background:#9F9;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-yes">Explicitly criminalised<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesthailand2017_Thailand]_567-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesthailand2017_Thailand]-567">[425]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>Rape is illegal,<sup id="cite_ref-AFPThailand_568-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AFPThailand-568">[426]</a></sup> although the government did not always enforce the law effectively. The law permits authorities to prosecute spousal rape, and prosecutions occurred. The law specifies penalties for conviction of rape or forcible sexual assault ranging from four years’ imprisonment to the death penalty as well as fines.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422125115httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017eap277121htm_Thailand]_569-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422125115httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017eap277121htm_Thailand]-569">[427]</a></sup> Marital rape was criminalised in 2007 amid strong controversy,<sup id="cite_ref-570" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-570">[428]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-571" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-571">[429]</a></sup> by Sec. 3(276) of the Penal Code Amendment Act (No. 19).<sup id="cite_ref-572" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-572">[law 143]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Togo" title="Togo">Togo</a> </td> 
         <td style="background:#9F9;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-yes">Explicitly criminalised<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiestogo2017_Togo]_573-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiestogo2017_Togo]-573">[430]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>Marital rape is explicitly criminalised by Arts. 211-212 of Loi No. 2015-010 Portant Nouveau Code Pénal<sup id="cite_ref-574" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-574">[law 144]</a></sup> and is punishable by up to 720 hours of community service and a fine of 200,000 to one million CFA francs.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422125123httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017af277057htm_Togo]_575-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422125123httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017af277057htm_Togo]-575">[431]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Tonga" title="Tonga">Tonga</a> </td> 
         <td style="background:#9F9;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-yes">Yes<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiestonga2017_Tonga]_576-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiestonga2017_Tonga]-576">[432]</a></sup> </td>
