         <td>The law recognizes spousal rape.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422125128httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017eap277125htm_Tonga]_577-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422125128httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017eap277125htm_Tonga]-577">[433]</a></sup> (Criminal Offences Act, Sec. 118(2)<sup id="cite_ref-578" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-578">[law 145]</a></sup> &amp; Family Protection Act, Sec. 29)<sup id="cite_ref-579" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-579">[law 146]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Trinidad_and_Tobago" title="Trinidad and Tobago">Trinidad and Tobago</a> </td> 
         <td style="background:#9F9;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-yes">Explicitly criminalised<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiestrinidad-and-tobago2017_Trinidad_and_Tobago]_580-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiestrinidad-and-tobago2017_Trinidad_and_Tobago]-580">[434]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>Marital rape was explicitly criminalised by section 4(4)(5) of the Sexual Offences (Amendment) Act, 2000.<sup id="cite_ref-581" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-581">[law 147]</a></sup> Rape is punishable by up to life imprisonment, but the courts often imposed considerably shorter sentences.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422125131httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017wha277363htm_Trinidad_and_Tobago]_582-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422125131httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017wha277363htm_Trinidad_and_Tobago]-582">[435]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Tunisia" title="Tunisia">Tunisia</a> </td> 
         <td style="background:#9F9;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-yes">Explicitly criminalised<sup id="cite_ref-583" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-583">[436]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>Prior to June 2017, marital rape was not considered a crime. Although Article 227 of the Penal Code does not exclude marital rape from its provisions, Article 23 of the Personal Status Code mandated partners in marriage to “fulfil their conjugal duties according to practice and customs,”<sup id="cite_ref-584" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-584">[437]</a></sup> On June 27, 2017, the <a href="/wiki/Assembly_of_the_Representatives_of_the_People" title="Assembly of the Representatives of the People">Tunisian Parliament</a> unanimously passed a comprehensive law addressing all forms of gender-based violence, including physical, economic, and social violence.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422125134httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017nea277267htm_Tunisia]_585-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422125134httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017nea277267htm_Tunisia]-585">[438]</a></sup> The provisions of this law include marital rape.<sup id="cite_ref-586" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-586">[439]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkey</a> </td> 
         <td style="background:#9F9;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-yes">Explicitly criminalised<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesturkey2017_Turkey]_587-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesturkey2017_Turkey]-587">[440]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>The law prohibits sexual assault, including rape and spousal rape (Art. 102, Criminal Code),<sup id="cite_ref-588" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-588">[law 148]</a></sup> with penalties of two to 10 years’ imprisonment for conviction of attempted sexual violation and at least 12 years’ imprisonment for conviction of rape or sexual violation.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422125136httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017eur277227htm_Turkey]_589-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422125136httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017eur277227htm_Turkey]-589">[441]</a></sup> Marital rape was criminalised in 2005.<sup id="cite_ref-UNTurkey_590-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UNTurkey-590">[442]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Turkmenistan" title="Turkmenistan">Turkmenistan</a> </td> 
         <td style="background:#9F9;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-yes">Yes </td> 
         <td>Marital rape is illegal and punishable by sentences ranging from 3 to 25 years imprisonment.<sup id="cite_ref-591" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-591">[443]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-592" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-592">[444]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Tuvalu" title="Tuvalu">Tuvalu</a> </td> 
         <td style="background:#F99;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-no">No<sup id="cite_ref-593" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-593">[445]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>Rape is a crime punishable by a minimum sentence of five years’ imprisonment, but spousal rape is not included in the legal definition of this offense.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422125145httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017eap277127htm_Tuvalu]_594-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422125145httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017eap277127htm_Tuvalu]-594">[446]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr>
       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="U">U</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Marital_rape_laws_by_country&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: U">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <table class="sortable wikitable"> 
       <tbody>
        <tr> 
         <th>Country </th> 
         <th>Criminalised </th> 
         <th class="unsortable">Notes </th>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Uganda" title="Uganda">Uganda</a> </td> 
         <td style="background:#F99;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-no">Customary law<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEThe_State_of_African_Women2018_595-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEThe_State_of_African_Women2018-595">[447]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>Rape is defined as “unlawful carnal knowledge of a woman or a girl without her consent”<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422125147httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017af277059htm_596-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422125147httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017af277059htm-596">[448]</a></sup> in Section 123 of the Penal Code, there is no marital exemption.<sup id="cite_ref-Benjamin_597-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Benjamin-597">[449]</a></sup> However, in <a href="/wiki/Customary_law" title="Customary law">customary law</a>, there is a presupposition that a woman implicitly consents to sexual intercourse with her spouse during marriage.<sup id="cite_ref-Benjamin_597-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Benjamin-597">[449]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-598" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-598">[450]</a></sup> As of late 2018,<sup id="cite_ref-599" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-599">[451]</a></sup> the Sexual Offences Bill, which would explicitly criminalise marital rape, is before the <a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_Uganda" title="Parliament of Uganda">Parliament of Uganda</a>. Similar bills were defeated in 1970, 2003 and 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-600" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-600">[452]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Ukraine" title="Ukraine">Ukraine</a> </td> 
         <td style="background:#9F9;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-yes">Yes<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesukraine2017_Ukraine]_601-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesukraine2017_Ukraine]-601">[453]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>The law prohibits rape of men or women but does not explicitly address spousal rape or domestic violence. The courts may use a law against “forced sex with a materially dependent person” as grounds to prosecute spousal rape.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422125151httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017eur277229htm_Ukraine]_602-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422125151httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017eur277229htm_Ukraine]-602">[454]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-603" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-603">[455]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/United_Arab_Emirates" title="United Arab Emirates">United Arab Emirates</a> </td> 
         <td style="background:#F99;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-no">No<sup id="cite_ref-604" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-604">[456]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-605" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-605">[457]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>The penal code does not address spousal rape. In October the Dubai Court of First Instance sentenced a policeman to six months in jail for raping his fiancée. The defendant argued that he considered the two married at the time of the offense.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422125154httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017nea277269htm_United_Arab_Emirates]_606-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422125154httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017nea277269htm_United_Arab_Emirates]-606">[458]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesunited-kingdom2017_United_Kingdom]_607-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesunited-kingdom2017_United_Kingdom]-607">[459]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td style="background:#9F9;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-yes">Court Decision<sup id="cite_ref-lords_608-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lords-608">[460]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>The law criminalises rape, spousal rape, and domestic violence. The maximum legal penalty for rape is life imprisonment. The law also provides for injunctive relief, personal protection orders, and protective exclusion orders (similar to restraining orders) for female victims of violence.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422125157httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017eur277233htm_United_Kingdom]_609-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422125157httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017eur277233htm_United_Kingdom]-609">[461]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Common_law" title="Common law">common law</a> presumption of a marital exemption was overturned by the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Lords" title="House of Lords">House of Lords</a> in the case of <i><a href="/wiki/R_v_R" title="R v R">R v R</a></i> in 1991.<sup id="cite_ref-lords_608-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lords-608">[460]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a> </td> 
         <td style="background:#9F9;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-yes">Yes<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesunited-states2017_United_States]_610-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesunited-states2017_United_States]-610">[462]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>
          <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
           Main article: <a href="/wiki/Marital_rape_(United_States_law)" class="mw-redirect" title="Marital rape (United States law)">Marital rape (United States law)</a>
          </div> Marital rape is illegal in all 50 <a href="/wiki/US_states" class="mw-redirect" title="US states">US states</a>. Legislation varies from state to state. </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Uruguay" title="Uruguay">Uruguay</a><sup id="cite_ref-611" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-611">[463]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td style="background:#9F9;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-yes">Yes<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesuruguay2017_Uruguay]_612-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesuruguay2017_Uruguay]-612">[464]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>The law criminalises rape of men or women, including spousal rape, although not explicitly (Código Penal, Art. 272).<sup id="cite_ref-613" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-613">[law 149]</a></sup> The law allows for sentences of two to 12 years’ imprisonment for a person found guilty of rape, and authorities effectively enforced the law.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422125200httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017wha277365htm_Uruguay]_614-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422125200httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017wha277365htm_Uruguay]-614">[465]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Uzbekistan" title="Uzbekistan">Uzbekistan</a> </td> 
         <td style="background:#9F9;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-yes">Explicitly criminalised<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesuzbekistan2017_Uzbekistan]_615-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesuzbekistan2017_Uzbekistan]-615">[466]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>Marital rape is explicitly criminalised by Art. 118 and Chapter Eight* of the Criminal Code,<sup id="cite_ref-616" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-616">[law 150]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-617" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-617">[467]</a></sup> however the courts did not try any rape cases as of 2017, according to human rights activists.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422125203httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017sca277299htm_Uzbekistan]_618-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422125203httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017sca277299htm_Uzbekistan]-618">[468]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr>
       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="V">V</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Marital_rape_laws_by_country&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: V">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <table class="sortable wikitable"> 
       <tbody>
        <tr> 
         <th>Country </th> 
         <th>Criminalised </th> 
         <th class="unsortable">Notes </th>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Vanuatu" title="Vanuatu">Vanuatu</a> </td> 
         <td style="background:#9F9;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-yes">Yes<sup id="cite_ref-619" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-619">[469]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>The Penal Code, Sec. 90,<sup id="cite_ref-620" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-620">[law 151]</a></sup> defines rape but does not explicitly include marital rape. Police are frequently reluctant to intervene in what they considered domestic matters.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422125208httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017eap277129htm_Vanuatu]_621-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422125208httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017eap277129htm_Vanuatu]-621">[470]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Venezuela" title="Venezuela">Venezuela</a> </td> 
         <td style="background:#9F9;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-yes">Explicitly criminalised<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesvenezuela-rb2017_Venezuela]_622-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesvenezuela-rb2017_Venezuela]-622">[471]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>Articles 15(7) &amp; 43 of the Ley Orgánica Sobre el Derecho de las Mujeres a una Vida Libre de Violencia (Organic Law on the Right of Women to a Life Free of Violence) explicitly criminalised marital rape in 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-623" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-623">[law 152]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Vietnam" title="Vietnam">Vietnam</a> </td> 
         <td style="background:#9F9;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-yes">Explicitly criminalised<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesvietnam2017_Vietnam]_624-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWomen,_Business_and_the_Law2018[httpwblworldbankorgendataexploreeconomiesvietnam2017_Vietnam]-624">[472]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>In 2002, marital rape was explicitly criminalised by article 2(1)(e) of the Law on Domestic Violence Prevention and Control.<sup id="cite_ref-625" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-625">[law 153]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr>
       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Y">Y</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Marital_rape_laws_by_country&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Y">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <table class="sortable wikitable"> 
       <tbody>
        <tr> 
         <th>Country </th> 
         <th>Criminalised </th> 
         <th class="unsortable">Notes </th>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Yemen" title="Yemen">Yemen</a><sup id="cite_ref-FBanda_184-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FBanda-184">[140]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-626" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-626">[473]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td style="background:#F99;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-no">No </td> 
         <td>The law criminalises rape, but it does not criminalise spousal rape because the law states a woman may not refuse sexual relations with her husband.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422125220httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017nea277273htm_Yemen]_627-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422125220httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017nea277273htm_Yemen]-627">[474]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr>
       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Z">Z</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Marital_rape_laws_by_country&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Z">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <table class="sortable wikitable"> 
       <tbody>
        <tr> 
         <th>Country </th> 
         <th>Criminalised </th> 
         <th class="unsortable">Notes </th>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Zambia" title="Zambia">Zambia</a> </td> 
         <td style="background:#9F9;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-yes">Explicitly criminalised<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422125223httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017af277061htm_Zambia]_628-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422125223httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017af277061htm_Zambia]-628">[475]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>The 2010 Anti-Gender-based Violence Act criminalises spousal rape.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422125223httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017af277061htm_Zambia]_628-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422125223httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017af277061htm_Zambia]-628">[475]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-629" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-629">[law 154]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td><a href="/wiki/Zimbabwe" title="Zimbabwe">Zimbabwe</a><sup id="cite_ref-SADC2007_630-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SADC2007-630">[476]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td style="background:#9F9;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center;" class="table-yes">Explicitly criminalised<sup id="cite_ref-The_State_of_African_Women_82-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_State_of_African_Women-82">[60]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-uneca_africa_225-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-uneca_africa-225">[174]</a></sup> </td> 
         <td>Marital rape was criminalised in 2004 by section 68 of the "Criminal Law (Codification And Reform) Act". However Article 68 (a) states "no prosecution shall be instituted against any husband for raping or indecently assaulting his wife .... unless the Attorney-General has authorised such a prosecution".<sup id="cite_ref-631" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-631">[law 155]</a></sup> Spousal rape receives less attention than physical violence against women.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422125225httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017af277063htm_Zimbabwe]_632-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECountry_Reports_on_Human_Rights_Practices2017[httpswebarchiveorgweb20180422125225httpswwwstategovjdrlrlshrrpt2017af277063htm_Zimbabwe]-632">[477]</a></sup> </td>
        </tr> 
       </tbody>
      </table>

Archived from <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.mdg5watch.org/index.php?option=com_content&amp;view=article&amp;id=93&amp;Itemid=155#_edn21">the original</a> on 27 December 2010<span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">8 March</span> 2011</span>. <q>China has no legal provisions for marital rape and the main reason for this is in deference to a prevailing cultural perception that wives are supposed to submit to their husband's wishes in matters of sexual relations and hence, there is no such concept of ‘rape’ within marriage or ‘rape’ being considered a form of violence within the marriage.</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.btitle=China%3A+MDG+3%3A+Promote+Gender+Equality+and+Empower+Woman&amp;rft.au=Asian-Pacific+Resource+and+Research+Centre+%28ARROW%29&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.mdg5watch.org%2Findex.php%3Foption%3Dcom_content%26view%3Darticle%26id%3D93%26Itemid%3D155%23_edn21&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AMarital+rape+laws+by+country" class="Z3988"></span>

         <li id="cite_note-535"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-535">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">South Sudan: <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.wipo.int/edocs/lexdocs/laws/en/ss/ss014en.pdf">Penal Code Act</a> (2008)</span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-540"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-540">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Sri Lanka: <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://hrlibrary.umn.edu/research/srilanka/statutes/Penal_Code.pdf">Penal Code</a> (1885, as amended)</span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-547"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-547">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Suriname: <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20140111205702/http://sgdatabase.unwomen.org/uploads/Suriname%20-%20Rev%20Moral%20Legislation%20(2009)%20(Dutch).pdf">Moral Law Amendment</a> (2009) <span class="languageicon">(in Dutch)</span></span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-549"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-549">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Sweden: <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.riksdagen.se/sv/dokument-lagar/dokument/svensk-forfattningssamling/brottsbalk-1962700_sfs-1962-700#K3">Penal Code</a> (1962, amended to 2018) <span class="languageicon">(in Swedish)</span></span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-553"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-553">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Switzerland: <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.admin.ch/opc/en/classified-compilation/19370083/201803010000/311.0.pdf">Criminal Code</a> (1937, amended to 2018)</span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-558"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-558">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Syria: <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.moj.gov.sy/index.php?option=com_content&amp;view=article&amp;id=11:2013-10-01-20-45-36&amp;catid=3:criminalgroup&amp;Itemid=6">Penal Code</a> <span class="languageicon">(in Arabic)</span></span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-561"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-561">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Taiwan: <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://law.moj.gov.tw/LawClass/LawAll.aspx?PCode=C0000001">Criminal Code of the Republic of China</a> <span class="languageicon">(in Chinese)</span></span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-566"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-566">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Tanzania: <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.ilo.org/dyn/natlex/docs/ELECTRONIC/67094/63635/F532037758/TZA67094.pdf">Sexual Offences (Special Provisions) Act</a> (1998)</span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-572"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-572">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Thailand: <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikisource.org/wiki/Translation:Penal_Code_Amendment_Act_(No._19)_2007#4">Penal Code Amendment Act (No. 19)</a> (2007)</span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-574"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-574">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Togo: <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.globalintegrity.org/wp-content/uploads/2016/08/Togo-Code-pe%CC%81nal-2015-.pdf">Loi No. 2015-010 Portant Nouveau Code Pénal</a> (2015) <span class="languageicon">(in French)</span></span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-578"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-578">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Tonga: <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://crownlaw.gov.to/cms/images/LEGISLATION/PRINCIPAL/1924/1924-0010/CriminalOffencesAct_1.pdf">Criminal Offences Act</a> (2016)</span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-579"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-579">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Tonga: <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20160304075338/https://crownlaw.gov.to/cms/images/LEGISLATION/PRINCIPAL/2013/2013-0018/FamilyProtectionAct2013_1.pdf">Family Protection Act</a> (2013)</span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-581"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-581">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Trinidad and Tobago: <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.ttparliament.org/legislations/a2000-31.pdf">Sexual Offences (Amendment) Act</a> (2000)</span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-588"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-588">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Turkey: <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://legislationline.org/download/action/download/id/6453/file/Turkey_CC_2004_am2016_en.pdf">Criminal Code</a> (amended to 2016)</span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-613"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-613">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Uruguay: <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://parlamento.gub.uy/sites/default/files/CodigoPenal2014-02.pdf?width=800&amp;height=600&amp;hl=en_US1&amp;iframe=true&amp;rel=nofollow">Código Penal</a> (amended to 2014) <span class="languageicon">(in Spanish)</span></span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-616"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-616">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Uzbekistan: <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.legislationline.org/download/action/download/id/1712/file/a45cbf3cc66c17f04420786aa164.htm/preview">Uzbekistan</a> (1994, amended to 2012)</span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-620"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-620">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Vanuatu: <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.paclii.org/vu/legis/consol_act/pc66/">Penal Code</a> (1981, amended to 2006)</span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-623"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-623">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Venezuela: <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.derechos.org.ve/pw/wp-content/uploads/11.-Ley-Org%C3%A1nica-sobre-el-Derecho-de-las-Mujeres-a-una-Vida-Libre-de-Violencia.pdf">Ley Orgánica Sobre el Derecho de las Mujeres a una Vida Libre de Violencia</a> (2007) <span class="languageicon">(in Spanish)</span></span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-625"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-625">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Vietnam: <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://moj.gov.vn/vbpq/en/Lists/Vn%20bn%20php%20lut/View_Detail.aspx?ItemID=3030">Law on Domestic Violence Prevention and Control</a> (2005)</span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-629"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-629">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Zambia: <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.ilo.org/dyn/natlex/docs/ELECTRONIC/90116/103668/F-846100824/ZMB90116.pdf">Anti-Gender-based Violence Act</a> (2011)</span> </li> 
         <li id="cite_note-631"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-631">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Zimbabwe: <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://archive.kubatana.net/docs/legisl/criminal_law_code_050603.pdf">Criminal Law (Codification And Reform) Act</a> (2004)</span> </li>
